
1

The Concept of Jivanmukti in Advaita And Other Topics

ShrIgurubhyo namaH
HariH Om
Recently I saw the following observation in the FAQ (Frequently Asked Questions) of
the site: www.dvaita.org.

Why does Tattvavâda deny jîvan-mukti?
//Because a mukta, or liberated person, should not even be physically present in the
material universe, unlike the un-liberated. A <span class="t0 t4 t5 t10 t22 t25 t28 hoverable">person</span> who is living in the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">world</span> cannot be
said to be <span class="t1 t8 hoverable">free</span> of sorrow <span class="t9 t24 hoverable">born</span> of material contact, and also cannot be said to experience
the joy of his own <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">nature</span> at all times. The very act of living in a gross material <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">body</span>
entails <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">things</span> such as eating, sleeping, pleasure and pain, etc., which cannot be accepted
in a mukta.
//The Advaitic concept of a jîvanmukta is also absurd because a <span class="t0 t4 t5 t10 t22 t25 t28 hoverable">person</span> who has
surmounted the realm of perception and realized the Absolute (as Advaita holds of a
mukta) should not continue to exist <span class="t0 t1 t4 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t23 t24 t25 t28 t29 hoverable">within</span> and interact with the realm of perception that
he has realized as being not-Real—no one continues to perceive a snake after realizing
that the <span class="t24 t25 hoverable">object</span> of his perception is actually a rope. The suggestion that such bondage to
the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">world</span> of perception continues for a while after the occurrence of Realization, because
of past attachments, is not tenable—such attachments themselves are artifacts of the
perceived <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">world</span> that has supposedly been sublated, and should not continue to besiege
the <span class="t0 t1 t13 t16 t24 t25 hoverable">consciousness</span> of the Realized. If they do, then we have to either reject the Realization
that is said to have occurred, or else reject the notion that the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">world</span> of perception, as
manifesting through the attachments on a supposedly Realized person, can be sublated.
In either instance, the notion of jîvanmukti is not meaningful. //
After reading the above, the following was <span class="t2 t11 t15 t19 t25 t27 hoverable">written</span> in the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">form</span> of mananam. The purpose
is to <span class="t5 t14 t15 t24 t27 hoverable">find</span> out how an advaitin <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">would</span> look at such an objection/opinion. In the process of
this exercise, some more topics were <span class="t2 t5 t11 t18 t19 t23 t26 hoverable">taken</span> up that are either directly or indirectly
connected with the main topic. As a result the document grew to its present size of 50
pages.It is possible that there are some repetitions of ideas/quotes.
Originally, there was no <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t17 t18 t20 t21 t23 t24 t25 t26 t28 hoverable">thought</span> of presenting this document to the organizers of the
Dwaita.org site. It was meant to be a study material for interested mumukshus. Owning
to the <span class="t7 t12 t13 hoverable">fact</span> that objections against Advaita arise due to inadequate grasping of the system
as it is taught and practiced in the sampradaya, I <span class="t2 t4 t6 t9 t18 t19 t22 hoverable">took</span> a decision to send the document to
the website so that the Advaitin’s perspective of various topics could be made known.
No criticism or counter-objections are intended in this attempt at dissemination of
knowledge. If this spirit, the one that could be seen in the recent Kannada <span class="t6 t8 t10 t11 t16 t20 t21 t27 t28 hoverable">book</span> ‘Mata

2
traya sameekshaa’ by Dr. A.V. Nagasampige, is had in mind, this document <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">would</span> have
served its purpose. The emphasis is mainly on explaining the stand of the Advaitin while
viewing the objections. It is possible that quotes in Sanskrit (Devanagari) lipi does not
come out in transmission. The references given <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">would</span> help in that case. Om Tat Sat.

The Explanation commences here:
In the Bhagavadgita, a ‘Tattavit’ is distinguished from the ignorant <span class="t0 t4 t5 t10 t22 t25 t28 hoverable">person</span> as:
prakṛteḥ kriyamāṇāni guṇaiḥ karmāṇi sarvaśaḥ
ahaṃkāravimūḍhātmā kartāham iti manyate 3.27
tattvavit tu mahābāho guṇakarmavibhāgayoḥ
guṇā guṇeṣu vartanta iti matvā na sajjate 3.28
Again, in the fifth chapter, we have the lakshana of a tattvavit described:
naiva kiṃcit karomīti yukto manyeta tattvavit
paśyañ śṛṇvan spṛśañ jighrann aśnan gacchan svapañ śvasan 5.8
pralapan visṛjan gṛhṇann unmiṣan nimiṣann api
indriyāṇīndriyārtheṣu vartanta iti dhārayan 5.9
The bodily acts of eating, sleeping, etc. are possible in the <span class="t5 t16 t21 t24 t25 hoverable">case</span> of a Tattvavit while
living, <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">without</span> the ‘aham karta’ bhava which is what is destroyed in the <span class="t5 t16 t21 t24 t25 hoverable">case</span> of the
tattvavit at the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">time</span> of realization, aparoksha jnanam, of the Atman/Brahman.
That such a <span class="t0 t1 t10 t14 t21 t23 t25 t29 hoverable">state</span> is admitted by the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> is evident from His words:
sarvakarmāṇi manasā saṃnyasyāste sukhaṃ vaśī
navadvāre pure dehī naiva kurvan na kārayan 5.13
yatendriyamanobuddhirmunir mokṣaparāyaṇaḥ
vigatecchābhayakrodho yaḥ sadā mukta eva saḥ 5.28
The mention of the ‘nine-gated city’ to mean that the Knower of the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Truth</span> still lives is
significant. And that such a knower, ‘does not do nor cause anything to be done’ is also
clear evidence for the released <span class="t0 t1 t10 t14 t21 t23 t25 t29 hoverable">state</span> while living which is <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">called</span> jivanmukti. All the
bodily functions can go on <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">without</span> hindering the vision of the Absolute that the liberated
<span class="t0 t4 t5 t10 t22 t25 t28 hoverable">person</span> has gained by dint of his sadhana. His is the <span class="t0 t1 t10 t14 t21 t23 t25 t29 hoverable">state</span> of ‘naishkarmyam’, the <span class="t0 t1 t10 t14 t21 t23 t25 t29 hoverable">state</span> of
Brahman. The other <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">verse</span> quoted above has Bhagavan’s own <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">words</span> that such a <span class="t0 t4 t5 t10 t22 t25 t28 hoverable">person</span> is
ever-liberated.

3
The lessons on samatvam, equanimity, in dvandvas like joy, sorrow, laabha, alaabha, etc.,
which are to be practiced by a sadhaka, when practiced adequately, remain in the tattvavit
even after gaining the aparoksha saakshatkara. So, when the body/mind complex is
subject to these dvandvas, owing to prarabdha karma, he remains unaffected as they
pertain to the deha/manas which are evolutes of prakriti, which the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> has taught as
anatma and the jnani has realized it to be so. If this were not to be so, the following
lakshanas of a ‘gunaatita’ will be questionable:
udāsīnavad āsīno guṇair yo na vicālyate
guṇā vartanta ity eva yovatiṣṭhati neṅgate 14.23
samaduḥkhasukhaḥ svasthaḥ samaloṣṭāśmakāñcanaḥ
tulyapriyāpriyo dhīras tulyanindātmasaṃstutiḥ 14.24
mānāpamānayos tulyas tulyo mitrāripakṣayoḥ
sarvārambhaparityāgī guṇātītaḥ sa ucyate 14.25
And also,
na prahṛṣyet priyaṃ prāpya nodvijet prāpya cāpriyam
sthirabuddhir asaṃmūḍho brahmavid brahmaṇi sthitaḥ 5.20
bāhyasparśeṣv asaktātmā vindaty ātmani yat sukham
sa brahmayogayuktātmā sukham akṣayam aśnute 5.21
ye hi saṃsparśajā bhogā duḥkhayonaya eva te
ādyantavantaḥ kaunteya na teṣu ramate budhaḥ 5.22
śaknotīhaiva yaḥ soḍhuṃ prāk śarīravimokṣaṇāt
kāmakrodhodbhavaṃ vegaṃ sa yuktaḥ sa sukhī naraḥ 5.23
yontaḥsukhontarārāmas tathāntarjyotir eva yaḥ
sa yogī brahmanirvāṇaṃ brahmabhūtodhigacchati 5.24
When is the ‘samachittatva’ practiced by the sadhaka put to test? Not when the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">body</span> is
not available. It is impossible to have dvandva anubhava in the absence of the body/mind
complex. The teaching of samachittatva becomes meaningful only in the possibility of
their (of dvandvas’) occurrence and the Jnani’s ability to remain equanimous. Being
affected by dvandvas is what samsara is and moksha is release from such identification
with dvandvas. This mochanam is what is demonstrated by the above verses. That is
why it is <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">called</span> jivanmukti.
The following verses of the VI <span class="t0 t2 t3 t4 t5 t8 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t20 t21 t23 t24 t26 t27 t28 hoverable">chapter</span> too throw much <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">light</span> on the topic. The <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">words</span>
‘brahmabhūtah’ is especially significant in that the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> says that such a yogi who is a
Tattvavit is ‘Brahman’ Itself. This is reminiscent of the Upanishadic statement: ‘brahma

4
veda brahmaiva bhavati‘. This is undoubtedly jivanmukti. The <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">words</span> ‘sarvathā
vartamānopi sa yogī mayi vartate 6.31’ bear <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">great</span> significance to the ‘actions’ of a Jnani.
In <span class="t5 t16 t21 t24 t25 hoverable">case</span> he is a grihastha, he will have to do the duties. In <span class="t5 t16 t21 t24 t25 hoverable">case</span> he is a sannyasi, there will
be no worldly duties. <span class="t0 t5 t8 t10 t14 t15 t21 t24 t28 hoverable">Whether</span> required to do duties or not, sarvathaa vartamaanopi, the
Jnani does not lose sight of the Absolute. Again the message of Jivanmukti is
unmistakable. The <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> says that such a mukta ever abides in Me, Brahman. When such
a Jnani is <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> Itself, where is the doubt that he is a mukta right now?
praśāntamanasaṃ hy enaṃ yoginaṃ sukham uttamam
upaiti śāntarajasaṃ brahmabhūtam akalmaṣam 6.27
sarvabhūtastham ātmānaṃ sarvabhūtāni cātmani
īkṣate yogayuktātmā sarvatra samadarśanaḥ 6.29
yo māṃ paśyati sarvatra sarvaṃ ca mayi paśyati
tasyāhaṃ na praṇaśyāmi sa ca me na praṇaśyati 6.30
sarvabhūtasthitaṃ yo māṃ bhajaty ekatvam āsthitaḥ
sarvathā vartamānopi sa yogī mayi vartate 6.31
ātmaupamyena sarvatra samaṃ paśyati yorjuna
sukhaṃ vā yadi vā duḥkhaṃ sa yogī paramo mataḥ 6.32
It is agreed that becoming affected by dvandvas is what constitutes samsara. So, the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span>
prescribes the sadhana of practicing equanimity in the <span class="t3 hoverable">face</span> of dvandvas. That means, as
<span class="t0 t1 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 hoverable">long</span> as the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">body</span> lives, dvandvas cannot be avoided or wished away. They keep coming
in turns. But the tattvavit who has become <span class="t1 t8 hoverable">free</span> from ignorance, ajnana, has gained the
ability to stand equanimous, unaffected, in the <span class="t3 hoverable">face</span> of dvandvas. Since the gunatita,
sthitaprajna lakshanas are prescribed, it obviously means that such a gunatita, tattvavit, is
still alive. For, there is no <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t10 t12 t13 t14 t15 t17 t20 t21 t23 t24 t25 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">meaning</span> in prescribing these lakshanas if there was no
possibility of a Jnani who has freed himself from samsara continuing to live in the body.
Since Jnana is the means to moksha and since moksha means release from samsara
caused by ajnana, jnanaprapti, and not death, means samsaarAt mochanam. That such a
mukta can be admitted to live till the fall of the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">body</span> is what is amply evidenced by the
verses on the gunatita/sthitaprajna. Dvandva-s, the other name for samsara, are unable to
affect this Jnani:
yadṛcchālābhasaṃtuṣṭo dvandvātīto vimatsaraḥ
samaḥ siddhāv asiddhau ca kṛtvāpi na nibadhyate 4.22
This is <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">called</span> Jivanmukti: Remaining unaffected by the dvandva-s. This is the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t10 t12 t13 t14 t15 t17 t20 t21 t23 t24 t25 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">meaning</span>
of moksha from samsara.
Thus, there is nothing unusual in the mukta purusha eating, sleeping, facing pleasure and
pain, etc. while being still embodied in the nava-dvara pura deha.

5
In the SrImadbhAgavatam, in the Jadabharata story, we <span class="t5 t14 t15 t24 t27 hoverable">find</span> a <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">verse</span> that talks of
jivanmukti:
-agvt pura[ pÂm> SkNx> àwmae=Xyay>
muKtae=ip taviÓ-&yaTSvdehmarBxmîÚi-manzUNy>,
ywanu-Ut< àityatinÔ> ik< TvNydehay gu[aÚ v&/<&&Ktee. 16.
(SrImadbhagavatam skandha 5, <span class="t0 t2 t3 t4 t5 t8 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t20 t21 t23 t24 t26 t27 t28 hoverable">chapter</span> 1, <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">verse</span> 16):
In the above <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">verse</span> (of <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> Brahmaa) the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">word</span> ‘Mukta’ is significant. The <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">word</span> ‘api’ is
even more significant in that it speaks of the ‘praarabdha karma phala’ for a Mukta which
is none other than jIvan mukti. The <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">word</span> ‘abhimAna-shUnyaH’ informs us that the
Mukta is devoid of attachment to the pleasure or pain the prarabdha karma brings to him.
In the <span class="t0 t2 t5 t13 t14 t16 t17 t20 t23 t24 t26 t28 t29 hoverable">second</span> line we have an interesting expression: ‘ yathAnubhUtam pratiyAtanidraH’ = the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">way</span> one who considers the dream experienced after waking up from sleep.
This is the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">way</span> the Jivanmukta, who having woken up to the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Truth</span> of the Non-dual
Brahman, perceiving the duality as a dream does not get attached to it knowing that it is
not real.
[One is reminded of the ideas contained in the ‘sAdhana-panchakam’ of Sri
Bhagavatpada Shankara. ‘prArabdham tu iha bhujyatAm…prAkkarma pravilApyatAm
chiti-balAt naapyuttaraiH shlishyatAm..’ conveying the message of the teaching of the
above verse.]
The <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Nature</span> of <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> is taught in the following verse:
-agvt pura[ pÂm> SkNx> Öadzae=Xyay>
}an< ivzuÏ< prmawRmekmnNtr< TvbihäRü sTym!,
àTyKàzaNt< -gvCDBds<}< yÖasudev< kvyae vdiNt. 11.
(SrImadbhagavatam skandha 5, <span class="t0 t2 t3 t4 t5 t8 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t20 t21 t23 t24 t26 t27 t28 hoverable">chapter</span> 12, <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">verse</span> 11):
In the above <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">verse</span> of Jadabharata to <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">King</span> RahUgana, the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">nature</span> of the Absolute <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Truth</span> is
being conveyed. It is Pure Consciousness, ParamArtham, Ekam, with no inside and
outside, <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t10 t12 t13 t14 t15 t17 t20 t21 t23 t24 t25 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">meaning</span> It is Non-dual, Impartite <span class="t0 t1 t13 t16 t24 t25 hoverable">Consciousness</span> which does not afford any
duality <span class="t0 t1 t4 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t23 t24 t25 t28 t29 hoverable">within</span> Itself or outside of Itself. It is Satyam. What is more? It is ‘pratyak’
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t10 t12 t13 t14 t15 t17 t20 t21 t23 t24 t25 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">meaning</span> ‘the Inmost <span class="t0 t1 t13 t16 t24 t25 hoverable">Consciousness</span> experienced by the jiva as ‘I’. In effect, the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">verse</span>
teaches that the ‘Tat’ is non-different from the ‘tvam’. This is the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">true</span> <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t10 t12 t13 t14 t15 t17 t20 t21 t23 t24 t25 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">meaning</span> of the
terms BhagavAn and Vaasudeva. Such is the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">way</span> the Seers (kavayaH) teach the Truth.
It is to be noted that the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">word</span> ‘ParamArtham’ means ‘Absolute Truth’. That means that
anything other than That is not the Absolute <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Truth</span> but is only in the relative plane. In
other <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">words</span> that which is not ParamArtha is only relatively real or mithyA.

From the various statements of the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> that He (the Lord, Brahman) is akarta and
abhokta and the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">true</span> <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">nature</span> of Atma (jiva) is also akarta and abhokta it is clear that what
differentiates a samsari from a mukta is the presence of the aham-karta/bhokta bhava and

6
its absence. To be akarta (eating, sleeping) and abhokta (sukha,dukha) one need not die.
Tattvavedanam destroys the kartritva/bhoktritva bhava. It does not destroy the prAna.
Nor does Tattvavedanam require prAna-tyaga to give its fruit of liberation. ‘Tam evam
vidvAn amrita iha bhavati’ says the Purusha Suktam. There is absolutely no difficulty
in explaining statements like:’ pretya asmAn lokAt amrutaa bhavanti’. ‘Loka’ is this
samsaric world. To ‘leave’ it is to render it powerless to affect the mukta purusha. To
disidentify oneself from the body/mind is what is moksha. This is enabled by aparoksha
jnanam. So, a jnani-mukta becomes amruta the moment the jnana dawns. One need not
die to become amruta.
//The Advaitic concept of a jîvanmukta is also absurd because a <span class="t0 t4 t5 t10 t22 t25 t28 hoverable">person</span> who has
surmounted the realm of perception and realized the Absolute (as Advaita holds of a
mukta) should not continue to exist <span class="t0 t1 t4 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t23 t24 t25 t28 t29 hoverable">within</span> and interact with the realm of perception that
he has realized as being not-Real—no one continues to perceive a snake after realizing
that the <span class="t24 t25 hoverable">object</span> of his perception is actually a rope. The suggestion that such bondage to
the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">world</span> of perception continues for a while after the occurrence of Realization, because
of past attachments, is not tenable—such attachments themselves are artifacts of the
perceived <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">world</span> that has supposedly been sublated, and should not continue to besiege
the <span class="t0 t1 t13 t16 t24 t25 hoverable">consciousness</span> of the Realized. If they do, then we have to either reject the Realization
that is said to have occurred, or else reject the notion that the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">world</span> of perception, as
manifesting through the attachments on a supposedly Realized person, can be sublated.
In either instance, the notion of jîvanmukti is not meaningful. //
Reply:
The realm of perception is the realm of Maya. That this Maya is ‘GunamayI’ is said by
the Lord. To ‘cross over Maya’ is to realize, first hand, that it is unreal. The practice for
that is to follow the ways of the Gunatita who considers, nay experiences, that the
function of perception, etc. are a play of Maya (gunA guneshu vartante/ indriyANi
indriyArtheshu vartante). The fruit of the practice is the aparoksha anubhava of the
Absolute in which realm there is no Maya. If total freedom from prakriti (identification
with the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">three</span> gunas) were an impossibility while the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">body</span> exists, the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">would</span> not
have prescribed the means for and stated the lakshanas of gunaatItatvam.
[In the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">verse</span> ‘DavI hyeShA gunamayI mama mAyA duratyayA/ mAmeva ye prapadyante
mAyAmetAm taranti te’ of the seventh ch. Gita, the ‘mAmEva’ means ‘ Me the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span>
alone with the exclusion of the mAyic world’. If one resorts to the Shuddha <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span>
alone <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">without</span> heeding to the mAyic duality, one can overcome the mAyic duality and
become freed. The freedom from mAyic <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">world</span> is taught in the Shruti: ‘BhUyashchaante
vishva-mAyA nivrittiH’. That the jivan mukta is freed from the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">world</span> created by mAya
is clear from these Shruti/Smriti statements.
That the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> is to be known as <span class="t1 t8 hoverable">free</span> from the guNas of Maya is also taught by the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span>
alone:
MAyA hyeShaa mayA sriShTa yan mAm pashyati naarada |

Sarvabhuta-guNairyuktam maivam mAm jnAtumarhasi || (Mahabharata/Vishnu
Puranam)
Here the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> instructs Sage Narada after showing him His VishvarUpa: This <span class="t0 t1 t2 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">form</span> of
mine, O Narada, is created by Me out of MAyaa. One should not know Me as endowed
with the guNas of the creation.
When one separates the gunas obtaining in creation, in other words, the entire creation,
from the Bhagavan, what we are <span class="t1 t7 t12 t29 hoverable">left</span> with is His shuddha, nirguna, svarUpam. This is
what is His Absolute Nature; the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">knowledge</span> of this is what is <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">called</span> ‘liberating
knowledge’. This is the Lord’s teaching that the <span class="t0 t1 t5 t7 t9 t11 t12 t13 t16 t17 t20 t23 t24 t26 t27 t29 hoverable">creation</span> is atAttvika, mAyika.]
To contend that ‘eating, sleeping, experiencing pleasure and pain, etc. are not possible for
a mukta who is alive in a body’ <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">would</span> <span class="t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t29 hoverable">land</span> one in a situation where Sri Rama and Sri
Krishna will have to be admitted to be baddha, ajnani samsaris. We have a <span class="t8 t21 t27 hoverable">number</span> of
instances recorded in the Gita/Mahabharata and the Valmiki Ramayana where eating,
sleeping, experience of pleasure and pain are associated with these <span class="t0 t1 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Divine</span> Incarnations.
For example in the Gita we have:
yac cāvahāsārtham asatkṛtosi
vihāraśayyāsanabhojaneṣu
ekothavāpy acyuta tatsamakṣaṃ
tat kṣāmaye tvām aham aprameyam 11.42
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> Krishna’s sleep and eating are mentioned here by Arjuna.
In the Mahabharata there is a description of the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> expressing His anguish and pain:
It is recorded in this <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Great</span> <span class="t6 t8 t10 t11 t16 t20 t21 t27 t28 hoverable">Book</span> that on learning of the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">death</span> of Abhimanyu, Arjuna
vowed that he <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">would</span> slay Jayadratha, who prevented the Pandavas from going to
Abhimanyu’s aid, by sunset on the next day, failing which he <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">would</span> immolate himself.
Krishna retired to His tent for the night after counseling Arjuna.
But in the middle of the night, Krishna woke up and remembering Arjuna’s vow told
Daruka (His charioteer) ‘O Daruka! Even for a moment, I cannot bear to see this <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">world</span>
bereft of Arjuna and the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">world</span> must not become so. For the sake of Arjuna, I will
quickly conquer and kill all of them, inclusive of Karna and Duryodhana, with their
horses and elephants. Let the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">three</span> worlds <span class="t2 t3 t4 t6 t7 t9 t11 t17 t18 t19 t20 t22 t26 hoverable">behold</span> tomorrow My prowess in the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">great</span>
battle…At daybreak after the expiry of this night, duly prepare My excellent chariot
according to the norms of warfare and follow Me. Equip it with the mace Koumodaki,
the <span class="t0 t1 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">divine</span> dart, Chakram, bow and arrows…..’ Several such instances can be cited from
the Mahabharata of Krishna behaving as if He lacked omniscience.
That the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> experienced pleasure needs no special mention. The Bhagavatam gives a
<span class="t8 t21 t27 hoverable">number</span> of instances of the Lord, as a lad, reveling with the other boys of Gokula and the
playing of pranks with the Gopis.
