Coming to the Ramayana, we have this instance, for example:
Rama was such an incarnation of Ishwara and so cannot have lacked the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">power</span> to know
what was pertinent. Yet, when Sita was abducted by Ravana, Rama searched for Her as
if He did not know Her whereabouts: Here is a translation of the concerned verses from
the Valmiki Ramayana:
‘Not seeing Sita there, having looked around, Rama <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">called</span> out with His beautiful arms
upraised and then said, ‘O Lakshmana! Where is Sita? Where has She gone from here?
By whom has She been abducted? Or by whom has My beloved been eaten? O Sita! If,
having hidden Yourself behind a tree, You wish to jest, enough of it today. Come to Me
who am very unhappy’….[He uses the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">words</span> ‘mAm suduHkhitam’] <span class="t1 t2 t3 t4 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t22 t23 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Together</span> with
Lakshmana, Rama began to search. The <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">two</span> scanned the forests, mountains, rivers and
ponds.’
There is an instance of Rama’s ‘sleeping’ recorded in the Ramayana:
/One day, when Rama and Sita were dwelling on the North-eastern base of the Chitrakuta
mountain, not far from the Ganges, a crow perched near Sita. She sought to drive the
bird away by hurling a clod of mud at it but it defiantly remained in Her vicinity.
Sometime later, as Rama slept on Her lap, the wicked bird sharply attacked Her breast.
Again and again it tore at her bosom and her blood wet Rama. She woke up Rama and
……./
There are instances of Rama ‘eating’ in the Ramayana. For example, Rama had vowed
not to <span class="t6 hoverable">eat</span> cooked <span class="t0 t14 t23 t24 hoverable">food</span> and sustain on fruits and roots gathered at the forest during His
vanavasa. Rama did not accept hospitality in Sugreeva’s palace. Rama did accept these
in the hermitages of Sages Sharabhanga, Agasthya, etc. <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Upon</span> hearing of the passing
away of Dasaratha from Bharata, Sri Rama performed the udaka/pinda kriya and then
partook of the <span class="t0 t14 t23 t24 hoverable">food</span> for the day.
There is the instance of His eating the berries offered by the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">great</span> devotee Shabari.
A question <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">would</span> arise: Rama and Krishna are Bhagavan, Ishwara, themselves in those
bodies. How can they be placed on par with the other jivas (muktas)? The former are
nityamuktas while the latter were baddha jivas and have attained the status later.
The above question is answered thus:
Although it might appear that there is a distinction, on closer analysis of the Gita and
other scriptures, it can be seen that Bhagavan Himself does not want to maintain such a
distinction. For example, in the Fourth <span class="t0 t2 t3 t4 t5 t8 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t20 t21 t23 t24 t26 t27 t28 hoverable">Chapter</span> the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> says:
janma karma ca me divyam evaṃ yo vetti tattvataḥ
tyaktvā dehaṃ punarjanma naiti mām eti sorjuna 4.9

9
The <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> says: Whoever realizes the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">truth</span> behind My ‘birth’ and ‘action’ as being of a
divine, MAyic, <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">nature</span> will attain moksha. How can the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">knowledge</span> of the mayic <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">nature</span> of
the Lord’s birth and actions <span class="t3 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t12 t13 t17 t18 t19 t20 t22 t23 t27 t29 hoverable">bring</span> about moksha to the knower? It is possible only in one
way: The knower, jiva, too realizes, on the basis of the teaching of the scriptures and the
Lord, that the birth and actions of himself too, are mayic alone and not real.
For example, the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> says in this <span class="t0 t2 t3 t4 t5 t8 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t20 t21 t23 t24 t26 t27 t28 hoverable">chapter</span> itself:
cāturvarṇyaṃ mayā sṛṣṭaṃ guṇakarmavibhāgaśaḥ
tasya kartāram api māṃ viddhy akartāram avyayam 4.13
na māṃ karmāṇi limpanti na me karmaphale spṛhā
iti māṃ yobhijānāti karmabhir na sa badhyate 4.14
First He says: Even <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">though</span> He has created this universe consisting of the four varnas, in
truth, He is akarta, non-doer. He is Eternal, Nirvikari (avyayam). And such a non-doer’s
(seeming) actions (naturally) do not bind Him. He further says: Whoever knows this
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">truth</span> (that the Lord, ParamAtma) Brahman, is a non-doer and that whatever He ‘does’ is
only seeming and <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">therefore</span> these ‘actions’ do not bind Him, will be freed from karma.
How is it possible that the knower of the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">truth</span> about Bhagavan’s actions becomes freed
from actions? This is possible under only one condition: Such a knower-jiva realizes that
even he is akarta in <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">truth</span> and even his actions are in <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">truth</span> not binding him.
In the II <span class="t0 t2 t3 t4 t5 t8 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t20 t21 t23 t24 t26 t27 t28 hoverable">chapter</span> of the Gita the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> has specified that the Atman is nitya, avadhya,
sanAtana, sarvagataH, achala, etc., all of which are applicable to <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> as well.
The essence of the above verses is: The <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> teaches that the jiva is non-different from
Brahman. There is nothing that can differentiate <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> from jiva excepting the
upadhis. When the upadhis are known to be false, mayic, the One Pure <span class="t0 t1 t13 t16 t24 t25 hoverable">Consciousness</span>
that is <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> and that is what the jiva is, alone remains as the Advaitam. (Shantam,
Shivam Advaitam of the Mandukya 7th mantra) and that is what the jiva is savrUpataH.
Thus, the ‘eating, sleeping, facing pleasure and pain’ cannot affect the nitya-mukta <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">nature</span>
of the jiva who has realized the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Truth</span> and continues in the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">body</span> for a while. These are
quite compatible with the mukta as they belong only to the asatya deha-mana-upadhis.
He has, by dint of the sakshatkara, freed himself from identifying with these upadhis.
There are a <span class="t8 t21 t27 hoverable">number</span> of Upanishadic passages that teach the non-difference of the Supreme
and the individual:
‘AtmA hyeShAm sa bhavati’(Br.Up.I.4.10) says that the Brahmavit who attains the
‘sarvabhAva’ (I am the All), is the AtmA, Self, of the devas.’ The context is <span class="t0 t5 t8 t10 t14 t15 t21 t24 t28 hoverable">whether</span> the
deva-s can create obstacles in the Jnani getting the phalam of jnanam namely moksha.
The Upanishat negates this possibility by asserting that since the Jnani, verily Brahman,
the sarvAtmA, is (also) the Self of the Deva-s, there cannot be any obstacle from the
devas in the Jnani’s liberation.

10

‘atha yo’nyAm devatAm upAste’nyo’sau aham anyo’smi iti na sa veda’ (Br.Up.I.4.10)
says: ‘He who worships another god, thinking, ‘He is one and I am another’ does not
know.’
‘udaram antaram kurute, atha tasya bhayam bhavati’ (Taittiriya Up. 2,7.1) says: ‘He who
conceives in terms of the slightest difference between himself and the Supreme, for him
there is fear.’
Whenever such a non-difference between the Supreme and the <span class="t22 t25 hoverable">individual</span> is taught, it
must be borne in <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">mind</span> that the identity is not with respect to the upadhis of the Supreme
and the individual. The Lord, in the Gita has given enough instances to show His <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">true</span>
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">nature</span> that is bereft of upadhis: For example:
na kartṛtvaṃ na karmāṇi lokasya sṛjati prabhuḥ
na karmaphalasaṃyogaṃ svabhāvas tu pravartate 5.14
nādatte kasyacit pāpaṃ na caiva sukṛtaṃ vibhuḥ
ajñānenāvṛtaṃ jñānaṃ tena muhyanti jantavaḥ 5.15
The <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> does not create agency or action in the jivas. Nor does He <span class="t3 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t12 t13 t17 t18 t19 t20 t22 t23 t27 t29 hoverable">bring</span> the jivas in
contact with their karma phalam. All these happen by the play of maya, avidya.
The <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> does not receive anyone’s <span class="t2 t5 t8 t17 t18 t19 hoverable">sin</span> or merit. These show that the Lord, in truth, does
not involve Himself in any of these functions related to the jiva-s. In the 14th ch. 19th
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">verse</span> He says that ‘Whoever realizes that there is no doer other than the guna-s and
knows the Self that is beyond the guna-s attains to My nature. This means that the
<span class="t22 t25 hoverable">individual</span> Self that is untouched by the guna-s is non-different from the Supreme Self
that is also untouched by the prakriti. It is in this <span class="t0 t1 t7 t12 t13 t14 t17 t23 t27 t28 hoverable">sense</span> that the identity is understood.
With prakriti as upadhi, the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> is sarvashakta and the <span class="t22 t25 hoverable">individual</span> is limited by nature.
Since this is the vyavaharic situation, the scriptures, alluding to this, teach the
paramarthic <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">truth</span> that is bereft of the upadhis. It is keeping in <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">mind</span> this <span class="t7 t12 t13 hoverable">fact</span> does the
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> say: ‘JnAnI tu Atmaiva me matam’ in the 7th <span class="t0 t2 t3 t4 t5 t8 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t20 t21 t23 t24 t26 t27 t28 hoverable">chapter</span> and ‘aham AtmA guDAkesha
sarvabhUtaashayasthitaH’ in the 10th chapter. In the former <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">verse</span> the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> says that the
Jnaani is verily Me and in the latter He says: ‘I am the pratyagAtmA of every being’.
What wonderful statements of abheda/aikyam/non-difference/identity!
The above verses may be contrasted with the Lord’s <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">words</span> showing His upAdhi-sahita
nature:
pitāham asya jagato mātā dhātā pitāmahaḥ
vedyaṃ pavitram oṃkāra ṛk sāma yajur eva ca 9.17
ahaṃ hi sarvayajñānāṃ bhoktā ca prabhur eva ca
na tu mām abhijānanti tattvenātaś cyavanti te 9.24
In these verses the ‘karma-phala-pra-vibhaktritva’, the ordainer-hood of the fruit of the
karma, is mentioned by the Lord. The <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> also says that He is the yajna-bhokta, the
receiver of the oblations offered. What is to be noted is, the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> denies that He is the

11
‘dhAtA’ and receiver of any punyakarma of the jiva-s in the verses shown in the earlier
paragraph.
The identity is <span class="t1 t3 t4 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t13 t15 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t27 t29 hoverable">brought</span> out by the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> in these verses too:
prakṛtyaiva ca karmāṇi kriyamāṇāni sarvaśaḥ
yaḥ paśyati tathātmānam akartāraṃ sa paśyati 13.29
[Here the Atma is said to be the non-doer. Who is this Atma? This is shown in the next
verse.]
yadā bhūtapṛthagbhāvam ekastham anupaśyati
tata eva ca vistāraṃ brahma saṃpadyate tadā 13.30
[The <span class="t0 t1 t13 t16 t24 t25 hoverable">Consciousness</span> that is non-doer, different-from-prakriti, is none other than Brahman,
the ‘Cause’ of the entire universe. This is the Atman, that is spoken of in the earlier
verse. The Chandogya Upanishad (VII.26.1) says: ‘AtmataH prANaH….’ meaning, from
Atman has emerged the entire universe. The Taittriya Up. says: ‘AtmanaH aakAshaH
sambhUtaH,…’. This Upanishat teaches: Brahmavit Apnoti param. Satyam Jnanam
Anantam Brahma. Where is this Atman/Brahman to be found and realized? ‘yo veda
nihitam guhAyAm parame vyoman’, It is available in the cave of the intellect. It is this
Consciousness, Atman, that is taught as the one beyond the five sheaths, koshas. It is this
<span class="t0 t1 t13 t16 t24 t25 hoverable">Consciousness</span> that every <span class="t22 t25 hoverable">individual</span> experiences as himself, although not knowing with
clarity. The teaching of the Upanishad that the Atman available in the cave of the
intellect is <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> is unmistakable. For, it says: He who knows the Atman in the cave
of the intellect is the knower of Brahman, Brahma-vit. Atmavit = Brahmavit. This
proves beyond doubt that there are no <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">two</span> consciousness-es, Atman and Brahman. This
is the One and Only <span class="t0 t1 t13 t16 t24 t25 hoverable">Consciousness</span> that is spoken of ‘…jnAnam, jneyam, jnAnagamyam, hRdi sarvasya vishthitam’ and ‘dhyAnena Atmani pashyanti kechit AtmAnam
AtmanA..’ (Gita 13th ch.) as available in the intellect of everyone, the kshetrajna, and as
that which is to be realized for securing liberation:
jyotiṣām api taj jyotis tamasaḥ param ucyate
jñānaṃ jñeyaṃ jñānagamyaṃ hṛdi sarvasya viṣṭhitam 13.17.
[The <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> has specified that the ‘jneyam’ is the anAdimat Param Brahma in this <span class="t0 t2 t3 t4 t5 t8 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t20 t21 t23 t24 t26 t27 t28 hoverable">chapter</span>
itself.]
This is the ‘kshetrajna’ in everyone which the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> taught as to be realized as He
Himself:
kṣetrajñaṃ cāpi māṃ viddhi sarvakṣetreṣu bhārata
kṣetrakṣetrajñayor jñānaṃ yat taj jñānaṃ mataṃ mama 13.2
This <span class="t0 t1 t13 t16 t24 t25 hoverable">Consciousness</span> is what is taught by the Brihadaranyaka Up.(III.7.4) as ‘yESha te
AtmA antaryAmyamRtaH’. ] [This is your Atma that is the antaryAmi, the <span class="t0 t28 hoverable">eternal</span> One.]
The teaching is: You, the Atma, is none other than the <span class="t0 t28 hoverable">Eternal</span> antaryAmin.]

12

In the Brihadaranyaka Up. there is the famous ‘Maitreyi Brahmanam’ where occurs the
teaching ‘Atmanastu kAmAya sarvam priyam bhavati’. Sage Yajnavalkya considers all
the possible objects that one desires and holds dear and finally concludes that all these
objects are dear only because they are subordinate to one’s own Self, Atman. This is
readily appreciable as it is so in our experience. Then the Sage goes on to say that this
Atman which is the dearest of all and is non-negotiable is the one to be known clearly,
i.e, <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">without</span> the admixture of the non-Atman, so as to result in attaining the summum
bonum of life. This Atma-jnanam is the mukti hetu. What is noteworthy here is that
there is no differentiation of Atman, the <span class="t22 t25 hoverable">individual</span> Self, from <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> the
Parameshwara. In the Kathopanishat, the very question of Nachiketas is about the
<span class="t22 t25 hoverable">individual</span> Self. While giving a detailed reply to this question, Yamadharmaraja explains
the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">nature</span> of Atman as non-different from Brahman. We are NOT <span class="t1 t7 t12 t29 hoverable">left</span> wodering <span class="t0 t5 t8 t10 t14 t15 t21 t24 t28 hoverable">whether</span>
it is Atma jnanam or Brahma jnanam that is moksha kAranam. All these point to the <span class="t7 t12 t13 hoverable">fact</span>
that there are no ‘two’ Atmans, jiva and Parama. It is One <span class="t0 t1 t13 t16 t24 t25 hoverable">Consciousness</span> only that is
spoken of in all the Upanishads as the Aupanishada Purusha. Atma sAkshAtkara is the
same as Brahma sAkshAtkara. The Kathopanishat mantra (II.i.1) ‘parAnchi khAni…..’
says: pratyagAtmaanam aikshat…amrutatvam icchan, meaning, pratyagAtma jnanam is
the liberating knowledge. This pratyagAtman is what is specified as the one transcending
the body-mind-ego complex as ‘tad vishnoH paramam padam’. <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Thus</span> it is settled beyond
doubt that the Atma of the jiva is none other than Brahman.
Who are we in truth?
To this question, generally we reply that we are the <span class="t0 t4 t5 t10 t22 t25 t28 hoverable">person</span> associated with a body, <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">mind</span>
and ego and related to various <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">people</span> and objects. Since this is not the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">truth</span> of our being,
as it is <span class="t9 t24 hoverable">born</span> out of avidya/adhyasa, the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> takes up the task of giving the teaching, in a
step-by-step manner.
The 13th <span class="t0 t2 t3 t4 t5 t8 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t20 t21 t23 t24 t26 t27 t28 hoverable">chapter</span> has these <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">two</span> verses even at the start:
śrībhagavān uvāca
idaṃ śarīraṃ kaunteya kṣetram ity abhidhīyate
etad yo vetti taṃ prāhuḥ kṣetrajña iti tadvidaḥ 13.1
The <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> says that the body-mind complex has to be separated from the Consciousness.
The ‘idam’, kshetram, the inert principle that is experienced as an object, vishaya, is to be
seen as different from the ‘aham’, the vishayi, the Consciousness, the kshetrajna. But, by
this much we are not given the entire picture. We have been taught what we are not.
What we are in <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">truth</span> is <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">yet</span> to be specified. To this end, the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> continues:
kṣetrajñaṃ cāpi māṃ viddhi sarvakṣetreṣu bhārata
kṣetrakṣetrajñayor jñānaṃ yat taj jñānaṃ mataṃ mama 13.2

13
The kshetrajna that is experienced in all of us as ‘I’ the Consciousness, is He Himself,
says the Lord. In effect, the teaching is: the ‘aham’ determined in the first <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">verse</span> is
‘Brahman’ as taught in the <span class="t0 t2 t5 t13 t14 t16 t17 t20 t23 t24 t26 t28 t29 hoverable">second</span> verse. Thus, in truth, we are Brahman.
We can arrive at the incontrovertible scriptural evidence for the jiva-Brahma abheda by a
short analysis:
The <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> says in the Gita:
idaṃ śarīraṃ kaunteya kṣetram ity abhidhīyate
etad yo vetti taṃ prāhuḥ kṣetrajña iti tadvidaḥ 13.1
kṣetrajñaṃ cāpi māṃ viddhi sarvakṣetreṣu bhārata
kṣetrakṣetrajñayor jñānaṃ yat taj jñānaṃ mataṃ mama 13.2
The point made in the first <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">verse</span> is: the mind-body, kshetram, is the vedya, ‘known’,
vishaya. The kshetrajna is the vEttA, the knower, vishayI principle. The kshetrajna is
the <span class="t0 t1 t13 t16 t24 t25 hoverable">Consciousness</span> available in the jiva chaitanyam and is <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">called</span> AtmA. This none can
deny as everyone experiences his body/mind as an object. This very <span class="t0 t2 t3 t4 t5 t8 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t20 t21 t23 t24 t26 t27 t28 hoverable">chapter</span> has a <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">verse</span>
that says that this is the Atman that is realized by the aspirant:
dhyānenātmani paśyanti kecid ātmānam ātmanā
anye sāṃkhyena yogena karmayogena cāpare 13.24
The point that is being made now is: Atman is the knower of the body-mind anAtman
kshetram.
We have in the Kenopanishat the following mantra:
Yan manasA na manute yEnAhur mano matam |
Tadeva Brahma tvam viddhi nedam yadidam upAsate || II.5 ||
[That which is not known by the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">mind</span> but by Which the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">mind</span> is known, know That to
be <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> …..]
Here, the Upanishad says that the <span class="t0 t1 t13 t16 t24 t25 hoverable">Consciousness</span> which knows the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">mind</span> as a vishaya is
Brahman. By juxtaposing the Gita verses above with this Kenopanishat mantra we
conclude that Atman, the knower of the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">mind</span> is otherwise <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">called</span> Brahman, the knower of
the mind. The result of this short analysis is: (jiva)Atman is (Para)Brahman. The <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span>
echoes the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">words</span> of this Kenopanishat mantra when He says: kṣetrajñaṃ cāpi māṃ
viddhi sarvakṣetreṣu bhārata. Kshetrajna Atma is Brahman, the Lord.
In the Taittiriyopanishat (Brahmaanandavalli – 1) we read: tasmAd vA EtasmAt
AtmanaH AkAshaH sambhUtaH….The <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">words</span> ‘tasmAt’ and ‘EtasmAt’ are significant in
the teaching of the Brahma-Atma abheda. ‘TasmAt’ is <span class="t0 t12 hoverable">used</span> when a distant, far-removed
entity is referred to. ‘EtasmAt’ is <span class="t0 t12 hoverable">used</span> to refer to an entity available close at hand,

14
proximate. The Upanishad referred to <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> by saying ‘satyam jnAnam anantam’.
The teaching is: ‘From That <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> that is verily This Atman the <span class="t0 t1 t5 t7 t9 t11 t12 t13 t16 t17 t20 t23 t24 t26 t27 t29 hoverable">creation</span> comes
forth…’ This is the Upanishadic <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">way</span> of teaching: <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> is Atman. The Mandukya
Upanishad too says: ‘ayam Atmaa Brahma’ by pointing to ‘this’ proximately known
Atman-Consciousness as Brahman. In the seventh mantra, after negating the jagat that is
the kArya, the Upanishat says: shAntam shivam advaitam (the jagat-kAranam divested of
the kAranatva status) is Atma. The adjective ‘shAntam’ of the TurIya in this Upanishat
could be seen as the ‘tadyaccet shAnta Atmani’ of the Kathopanishat where the Atman is
the pratyagAtman alone, undoubtedly. This Atman is the innermost, guhA-hitam, beyond
the mind, intellect, ego. <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Thus</span> the TurIya <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> is Shantam and the pratyagAtman
available in the jIva is also shAntam. The purport of the Upanishads is in teaching that
the jiva-Consciousness is <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> indeed.
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Yet</span> another Upanishadic reference to the above <span class="t23 hoverable">kind</span> of teaching is to be found in the
Kathopanishad II.i.10:
//Yadeveha tadamutra yadamutra tadanviha. Mrutyo: sa mrutyumApnoti ya iha nAneva
pashyati//
That which is Here (in this body, the microcosm) is what is present There (Macrocosm,
the All-pervading Tat, Brahman). That which is There is what is available in this <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">body</span> as
the Chaitanyam. One who misses this identity remains in samsara.
While teaching the Jneyam, Brahman, the Gita 13th ch. says:
sarvataH paaNi-pAdam tat sarvatokshi-shiro-mukham |
sarvataH shrutimat loke sarvamAvritya tishthati ||
This <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">verse</span> says that <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> is what is appearing as all the <span class="t1 hoverable">physical</span> bodies everywhere.
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> is what is pervading everything in the world. By saying this, the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> says that
the chaitanyam obtaining in every <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">body</span> is Brahman.
It could be objected: What the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> is teaching is that the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> is all the <span class="t1 hoverable">physical</span> bodies;
the chaitanyam indwelling the bodies are different jiva-s.
Reply: If this is admitted, then the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">would</span> be subjected to all the properties of
<span class="t1 hoverable">physical</span> bodies like birth, growth, old age, disease, decay and death. Contrary to this the
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> has taught that the Atman/Brahman is ajam, nityam, shAshvatam, nirvikAri, etc.
Moreover, the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> has also taught that the entire kshetram consisting of the <span class="t1 hoverable">physical</span>
bodies, the subtle bodies (mind), etc. are distinct from the Kshetrajna, the Sakshi
Chaitanyam, obtaining in all bodies. Not only that, the kshetram is to be separated, by
viveka, from the kshetrajna and the separated kshetrajna is to be realized as one’s
Self/Brahman, for liberation to ensue. <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Thus</span> the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t10 t12 t13 t14 t15 t17 t20 t21 t23 t24 t25 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">meaning</span> of the above <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">verse</span> is that it is
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> that is available in each <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">body</span> as the chaitanya. The bodies consisting of hands,
feet, etc. are identification marks for locating the shuddha chaitanyam which is not
available for sensory perception. In the Taittiriya Upanishat, BhruguvallI, we <span class="t5 t14 t15 t24 t27 hoverable">find</span> that the
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">father</span> VaruNa employs this method. He teaches after saying ‘tapasA brahma
vijijnAsasva [realize <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> through intense meditative enquiry], that the doorways to

15
search for <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> are: annam, prANam, chakshuH, shrotram, mano vAcham iti’ [the
activities seen in the jiva in the gross body, the prana, the seeing, hearing, thinking,
speech, etc. are the identification marks by which one ascertains that the Brahma
chaitanyam is present]. It is like specifying a residence with a particular address to locate
the <span class="t22 t25 hoverable">individual</span> who resides there. TheTaittiriya Up.says: ‘tat shrushtvA
tadevAnuprAvishat’: Having created the bodies, <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> entered these bodies as jiva-s
and is available in the bodies as the karta, bhokta, jnAta, manta, etc. That is why the
Upanishad says: yo veda nihitam guhAyAm …so’shnute sarvAn kAmAn saha brahmanA
vipashchitaa….whoever realizes the chaitanyam enshrined in the cave of the intellect as
his self/Brahman attains pUrnatva and is liberated. This ‘residing in the cave of the
intellect’ is what is meant by the ‘pravesha’ of <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> into the bodies which is termed
kshetram/anAtmA/prakriti, etc. The 13th ch. teaches that the Purusha/Brahman resides in
the prakriti/body and experiences, out of ignorance, the guna-s <span class="t9 t24 hoverable">born</span> of prakriti. The
separating, through viveka, from prakriti is what constitutes liberation.
The above <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">verse</span> also proves the scriptural teaching of jiva-Ishwara abheda.
The above analysis, incidentally, provides the answer to a possible objection, arising out
of not grasping the Advaitic/Upanishadic teaching correctly: How can there be pUrNatva
to the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> which is said to be conditioned by MAyA (MAyAvacchinnasya
BrahmanaH katham pUrNatvam upapadyate)? The reply is: The conditioning in the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">form</span>
of residing in the body/mind complex is not Absolute but is only incidental, Avidyaka.
When by taking recourse to sadhana based on the Guru-Shastra upadesha one realizes
that the sAkshi chaitanyam obtaining in the guhA = intellect is the akhanda Brahma
chaitanyam, the avidya conditioning is destroyed and the native pUrnatvam is realized as
‘I have ever been PUrNa’.
Is the realization in the manner ‘aham Brahma asmi’ an expression of arrogance?
There is an impression among the theistic schools, who are unable to arrive at the prime
purport of the Vedanta, that the Advaitin’s interpretation of Upanishadic teachings ‘Tat
tvam asi’, ‘Aham Brahma asmi’, etc. amount to an expression of arrogance on the part of
one who teaches so and the one who realizes so. That such a <span class="t25 hoverable">view</span> is founded on
ignorance is not difficult to understand. The Mandukya Upanishad teaches: ‘shAntam
shivam advaitam, sa Atma, sa vijneyaH’ [the TurIya is Peace Supreme, Auspiciousness
and Non-dual. It is the Self and has to be realized (for liberation)] The Kathopanishad
teaches: ‘tad vishnoH paramam padam’ when specifying the transcendental <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">nature</span> of the
Absolute Truth. The Chandogya Upanishad teaches: ‘tat satyam, sa Atma, tat tvam asi’
[That is the ever-existent Truth, It is the Self, That <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">thou</span> art]. The Brihadaranyaka
Up.teaches: ‘tat AtmAnam eva avet aham brahma asmi iti’ [It realized Itself as ‘I am
Brahman’]. This very Upanishad (IV.iv.13) teaches the mode of realization of the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Truth</span>
thus:
AtmAnam ched vijAnIyAt ayam asmi iti pUrushaH |
Kim icchan kasya kAmAya sharIram anu sanjwaret ||

16
The teaching here is: whoever realizes the Atma, self, as ‘this Atma, am I’ no longer
remains in embodied nature.
We find, in the above instance, such an ‘anvaya’ (positive) <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">way</span> of teaching by the Shruti
as to ‘how’ the realization aught to be. We also <span class="t5 t14 t15 t24 t27 hoverable">find</span> the ‘vyatireka’ <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">way</span> of teaching by
the Shruti as to ‘how not’ the realization aught to be. For example: the Brihadaranyaka
Up. I.iv.10 teaches: ‘atha yo anyAm devatAm upAste “anyo asau anyo aham asmi” iti
na sa veda yathaa pashurevam sa devaanAm’. Whoever worships/contemplates any deity
with the attitude: ‘This deity is different and I am different’ does so in ignorance; he is
indicted as a slavish animal to the deity’. The purport of the ‘anvaya’ and ‘vyatireka’
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">way</span> of teaching is that: Atman/Brahman is to be realized as oneself only and not
otherwise.
Apart from this, those who advance the ‘arrogance’ <span class="t25 hoverable">view</span> fail to see that when the Shastra
teaches abheda saakshAtkAra, it is not doing it in the level of the body-mind
identification. It teaches first the method of dissociating the Consciousness, the Self,
from the superimposed not-self consisting of the body-mind (through the pancha-kosha
viveka, avasthAtraya viveka, etc). Doing this at the <span class="t22 t25 hoverable">individual</span> level is not enough. The
separating of the upadhis from the Cosmic Self, Brahman, is also required. This is done
by negating the creatorhood, managerhood, etc. of <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> and seeing just the Pure
Consciousness. The Mandukya Upanishad does this admirably. After teaching the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">nature</span>
of the <span class="t22 t25 hoverable">individual</span> self and Cosmic Self with the upadhis in the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">three</span> pAda-s, vishva-virAt,
taijasa-hiranyagarbha and prAjna-Ishwara, the Upanishad embarks on the exercise of
negating all the upadhis (of both the <span class="t22 t25 hoverable">individual</span> and the Supreme Self) in the seventh
mantra: ‘na antaH prajnam…., etc’. What remains as unnegatable finally is: ShAntm
Shivam Advaitam. This Truth, the Upanishad says: ‘sa AtmA, sa vijneyaH’ is the Self
that has to be realized.
In the Bhagavad Gita too we can discern this method. For example, in the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">verse</span> of the
13th chapter: ‘kshetrajnam cha api mAm viddhi’ the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> is not equating the body-mindupadhi-jiva with Himself. He separates the kshetrajna, the Consciousness, Knower, from
the kshtra, the inert principle, the known. It is only after separating the body-mind
complex from the chaitanyam does the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> teach the aikyam. On the part of the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span>
too, we can determine from the various other verses that He is the <span class="t0 t1 t13 t16 t24 t25 hoverable">Consciousness</span> that is
‘akartA’, ‘avyaya’, ‘na cha matsthAni bhUtaani’ etc.
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Thus</span> the abheda, aikyam, taught by the Shastra is only in the level of Pure
Consciousness, the nirupAdhika chaitanya. In the sopaadhika chaitanya no aikyam is
possible. The accusation of ‘arrogance’ might be valid only when someone claims he is
Brahman/Ishwara <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">without</span> giving up the body-identification.
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Thus</span> we see that the Upanishad itself is instructing/prescribing the mode of realization of
the liberating <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">truth</span> as ‘I am this Atma/Brahman’. To maintain that this is arrogance on
the part of the teacher and the sadhaka is to impute the Upanishad itself of perpeterating
arrogance.

17
<span class="t1 t11 t16 t20 t25 t27 t28 hoverable">Reason</span> too supports that <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">true</span> liberation ensues from the realization of the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Truth</span> as ‘I am
Brahman’. <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> is said to be ‘amRta’, untouched by death. Liberation is freedom
from the cycle of births and deaths. It is only he who gains the conviction, through direct
experience, that he is <span class="t1 t8 hoverable">free</span> from <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">death</span> attains to the <span class="t0 t1 t10 t14 t21 t23 t25 t29 hoverable">state</span> of liberation which is <span class="t1 t8 hoverable">free</span> from
death. To this end, it is not sufficient if one realizes that ‘Bhagavan/Atman/Brahman is
amRta svarUpa’ and conclude ‘I am different from Bhagavan/Brahman/Atman’. The
notion <span class="t9 t24 hoverable">born</span> of ignorance: ‘I am a samsari, subject to birth and death’ can go only when it
is replaced by the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">knowledge</span> arising out of the appropriate Pramana: ‘I am not a samsari,
I am amRta, amaraNadharmA’. My realizing that some one other than me is amRta will
not confer on me the liberation from death/samsara. There are a <span class="t8 t21 t27 hoverable">number</span> of Upanishadic
passages that declare the realization of an aspirant:
It is reported in the Taittiriya Upanishad, sIkshAvallI (I.x.1): ‘aham vRkshasya rerivaa,
kIrthiH pRShTham gireriva..sumedhA amRtokshitaH’ [ ‘I am the invigorator of the tree
of samsara. My fame is <span class="t17 t29 hoverable">high</span> like the ridge of a mountain….I am soaked in nectar. <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Thus</span>
was the statement after the realization of the unity of the Self expressed by Sage
Trishanku] . ). In the <span class="t5 t16 t21 t24 t25 hoverable">case</span> of Sage Trishanku’s declaration the Taittiriya Up. itself says:
‘iti Trishankor-veda-anu-vachanam’ meaning: This declaration of Trishanku is in
accordance with the Veda.
‘ahamannam ahamannam….’ is the declaration of the realization of the sarvAtma bhAva
by Bhrigu in the Taittiriya Upanishad (III.x.5-6).
We have in the Aitareya Upanishad the declaration of sage Vaamadeva which is
unmistakably his realization of SarvAtmabhAva and release from bondage that existed
previously.
The Brihadaranyaka Upanishad (I.iv.9) raises a question:
//tadAhuH, yat ‘BrahmavidyayA sarvam bhavishyantaH’ manushyAh manyante, kimu
tad brahma avEt yasmAt tat sarvam abhavat iti//
[They say: <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Men</span> think, ‘Through the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">knowledge</span> of <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> we shall become all.’ Well,
what did that <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> know by which It (Brahman) became all?]
Replying this question, the Upanishad itself says in the very next mantra: (I.iv.10):
//Brahma vA idamagra AsIt…’aham BrahmAsmI iti.’ TasmAt tat sarvam abhavat…//
[This (self) was indeed <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> in the beginning. It knew only Itslef as ‘I am Brahman.’
And thereby It became All.]
In <span class="t25 hoverable">view</span> of all this, it <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">would</span> be un-upanishadic not to attain the liberating <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">knowledge</span> as: ‘I
am Brahman’. A realization not in accordance with this <span class="t0 t1 t2 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">form</span> will not result in liberation,
anirmoksha-prasangaH.

18
It might appear that the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> does <span class="t25 hoverable">view</span> those who have refused to come to Him as being
<span class="t0 t28 hoverable">eternal</span> sinners. The verse:
tān ahaṃ dviṣataḥ krurān saṃsāreṣu narādhamān
kṣipāmy ajasram aśubhān āsurīṣv eva yoniṣu 16.19
could give an impression that the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> sees these <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">people</span> as different from Him and that is
the <span class="t1 t11 t16 t20 t25 t27 t28 hoverable">reason</span> He consigns them to <span class="t0 t28 hoverable">eternal</span> hells. This <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">verse</span> has to be seen in the background
of the other verses where the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> says that He neither takes anybody’s <span class="t2 t5 t8 t17 t18 t19 hoverable">sin</span> or merit, nor
does He brings about the connection between the jiva-s and their karma-phala; it is the
svabhAva, prakriti, that operates and the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> has nothing to do with this. Also, the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span>
has said that those who come close to Him get the benefit of His care and those who
choose to remain away from Him do not get this benefit. Here too, the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> remains
unattached, asanga; the actions of the jiva-s <span class="t3 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t12 t13 t17 t18 t19 t20 t22 t23 t27 t29 hoverable">bring</span> about the respective fruits.
Understanding ‘ahankaara’ (a possible synonym for ‘arrogance’):
Much of the confusion arises because of not analyzing the ‘I’, ‘aham’ concept. The
scriptures and the ShaastrakAra-s have <span class="t2 t5 t11 t18 t19 t23 t26 hoverable">taken</span> pains to do this exercise with a <span class="t25 hoverable">view</span> to
<span class="t3 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t12 t13 t17 t18 t19 t20 t22 t23 t27 t29 hoverable">bring</span> about a proper understanding of the ‘I’ concept. For example in the Yoga
VAsishTha (Reference: ) Sage VasishTha instructs Sri Rama:

[Raghava! In all the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">three</span> worlds the ‘I’ <span class="t0 t1 t7 t12 t13 t14 t17 t23 t27 t28 hoverable">sense</span> is three-fold. Of these <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">two</span> are virtuous and
the <span class="t26 hoverable">third</span> is to be given up. Hear now the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">three</span> types:

19

‘I am the Supreme Self, the entire Universe and nothing else exists apart from Me.’ Such
a right <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">knowledge</span> consists of the Supreme I-sense.
‘I am different from everything else and am extremely subtle, even than the tip of the hair
of a tail.‘ This <span class="t23 hoverable">kind</span> of right <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">knowledge</span> is the <span class="t0 t2 t5 t13 t14 t16 t17 t20 t23 t24 t26 t28 t29 hoverable">second</span> type of virtuous I-sense.
The certitude of the <span class="t23 hoverable">kind</span> ‘I am a mere collection of hands, feet and other organs’ is the
<span class="t26 hoverable">third</span> type of I-sense which is of the ignorant <span class="t23 hoverable">kind</span> and is lowly.
O Sinless One, if someone contemplates for <span class="t0 t1 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 hoverable">long</span> on the first <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">two</span> types of I-sense that
constitutes virtue, he reaches the Supreme Lord.]
(Note: While the first type is typical of the Advaitic sadhana, the <span class="t0 t2 t5 t13 t14 t16 t17 t20 t23 t24 t26 t28 t29 hoverable">second</span> type could be
viewed as typefying the Bhakti sadhana of the Dwaita/Vishishtadwaita schools.)

The Panchadashi of Swami Vidyaranya too enumerates the types of I-sense. Says the
<span class="t0 t2 t3 t4 t5 t8 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t20 t21 t23 t24 t26 t27 t28 hoverable">Chapter</span> VI (TRptideepa slokas 9 - 13) in this connection:

[Question: In the Pure <span class="t0 t1 t13 t16 t24 t25 hoverable">Consciousness</span> that is unattached with anything else, how can there
exist the I-sense?
Reply: There can be <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">three</span> types of I-senses of which one is primary and the other <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">two</span> are
secondary. The primary one is the result of the mutual superimposition of the
Unchanging Self and the reflected <span class="t0 t1 t13 t16 t24 t25 hoverable">Consciousness</span> (body-mind complex). This admixture
is the one identified with by the ignorant people. (Being resorted to by most people, it is
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">called</span> ‘primary’.)

20
The Jnani, Knower, however, separates the Unchanging Self from the reflected
<span class="t0 t1 t13 t16 t24 t25 hoverable">Consciousness</span> and identifies with both of the I-senses, in a ‘toggling’ manner, while
engaging in worldly and <span class="t0 t4 t6 t7 t8 t11 t14 t16 t17 t21 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">spiritual</span> parlances.
As to how he does this is explained thus:

l]Oi¿¿vy]v]h]re%h\g]cC]m]Ity]]id¿† b¶D]: |

|

13 ||
In worldly vyavahara such as ‘I an going to…’, the Knower separates the reflected
<span class="t0 t1 t13 t16 t24 t25 hoverable">Consciousness</span> (from the Pure Consciousness) and uses the ‘I’ in this sense.
When engaging in contemplating <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">upon</span> the Pure <span class="t0 t1 t13 t16 t24 t25 hoverable">Consciousness</span> as ‘I am the unattached
Self, the Pure Consciousness’, the Knower uses the I-sense in the Pure Self.]
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Thus</span> one can see that the Vedic teaching of the manner of realization of the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Truth</span> in the
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">form</span> of ‘Aham Brahma asmi’ is conveyed by the Acharyas to the aspirant most carefully
by giving no room for any ‘arrogance’ in the process.
Are we many?

Having seen that the jiva-Ishwara bheda is founded on false knowledge, let us examine
the jiva-jiva bheda. We have the experience, ‘I am different from the others’. Each of us
swears that he is undoubtedly a conscious being. Is this not proof of our being different
individuals? To such a question, the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> replies:
In the 13th <span class="t0 t2 t3 t4 t5 t8 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t20 t21 t23 t24 t26 t27 t28 hoverable">chapter</span> there is a verse:
avibhaktaṃ ca bhūteṣu vibhaktam iva ca sthitam 13.16
The <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> says that Brahman, Consciousness, is not divisible; It cannot be fragmented and
distributed in each individual. But it appears to be divided in various individuals. The
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> uses the particle ‘iva’ to denote the seeming <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">nature</span> of such a division. The Shruti
‘Nishkalam…’ denies parts or amsha-s in Brahman/Atman. Admitting amsha-s in
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> is against other shruti teachings like ‘vijnaana ghanaH’, ‘ekam eva advitIyam’,
‘ajam, avyayam’,etc. Smriti, the Gita, too is against this contention. The Sutra ‘avibhAgo
vachanAt’ IV.ii.16 also denies any vibhaaga, kalaa, amsha, in <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> in the absolute
state. The Prashna Up. VI.5 states: ’ bhidyete tAsAm nAmarUpe.sa esho a-kalo amruto

21
bhavati’. That which is made up of parts is essentially a created one and not ajam. When
the parts, amshas, disintegrate, the ‘whole’, amshI, faces destruction. Then, what is the
basis of our ‘holding’ that we are all different individuals? The reply is: We see the
different bodies and get deluded that we are different individuals. Deha-nAnaatva is
mistaken for chaitanya nAnAtva. Since each of us has, due to adhyasa, conceived a <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">body</span>
which is finite, paricchinna and apUrna, we conclude that each is a finite, different
individual. The kshetram does not subsist in the <span class="t0 t1 t10 t14 t21 t23 t25 t29 hoverable">state</span> of Moksha; it is separated from the
Purusha and discarded. So, it <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">would</span> be wrong to hold that the Mukta will continue to
have a distinct entity of his own from the others, either while alive or after the fall of the
body. All distinguishing factors belong to the kshetram/prakriti alone and the
Purusha/Brahman is untouched by this.
Then what about the Lord’s other statements where there is a clear indication of many
jivas?
natv evāhaṃ jātu nāsaṃ na tvaṃ neme janādhipāḥ
na caiva na bhaviṣyāmaḥ sarve vayam ataḥ param 2.12
[That the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> is using the plural <span class="t8 t21 t27 hoverable">number</span> having in <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">mind</span> the various bodies that are
experienced in the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">world</span> but He has not conveyed that the jeeva-s are many in <span class="t8 t21 t27 hoverable">number</span> in
the pAramArthic/absolute <span class="t0 t1 t7 t12 t13 t14 t17 t23 t27 t28 hoverable">sense</span> can be understood by examining some other verses.
A <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">verse</span> (32) occurring in the 11th chapter:
‘….Rte’pi tvAm na bhavishyanti sarve ye….yodhAH’
[Even <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">without</span> you(r effort to slay them) these warriors will not survive]
Here, the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> shows how the rule: ‘jAtasya hi dhruvo mRtyuH’ (II. 27) ‘death is certain
for one who is born’ is infallible. In the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">verse</span> we saw above (II.12) He avers the other
side of this rule: ‘dhruvam janma mRtasya’ ‘Birth is certain for the one who dies’. Thus,
in <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">order</span> to <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">take</span> another birth, the departed souls (note plural) have to exist. It is only the
realized one, Mukta, that does not <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">take</span> another birth after the <span class="t1 hoverable">physical</span> <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">body</span> dies.
Again,
antavanta ime dehAH nityasyoktaH sharIriNaH |
anAshino aprameyasya ………………………….|| 2.18
Here too, we see the plural <span class="t8 t21 t27 hoverable">number</span> with reference to the bodies. But the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> does not
<span class="t1 hoverable">use</span> the plural to denote the indweller of the bodies: sharIri. He qualifies the sharIri as
Nitya, anAshI and aprameya. The <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> had taught what the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">true</span> <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">nature</span> of the sharIri is in
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">verse</span> 2.17 as ‘avinAshI’ and who pervades ALL THIS <span class="t0 t1 t5 t7 t9 t11 t12 t13 t16 t17 t20 t23 t24 t26 t27 t29 hoverable">CREATION</span> and this entity is
beyond destruction by any force.
Here we have in clear terms that the Self, Atman, about <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t11 t12 t13 t14 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">whose</span> <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">true</span> <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">nature</span> the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> is
teaching Arjuna in the wake of his despondency, is One only and that It is All-pervading.
An additional point to be noted in <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">verse</span> 2.18 is: All the(se) bodies are the various

22
manifestations of the One sharIri alone; the shashThee vibhakti makes this clear beyond
doubt. The ultimate teaching is: One Self and several bodies.
The above is corroborated through the Lord’s own <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">words</span> in the 13th chapter:
Kshetrajnam cha api mAm viddhi sarva kshetreshu bhArata
Know Me to be the SharIri obtaining in every body. (An aside point: the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">word</span>
‘kshetram’ cannot mean ‘the entire world/creation’ ; it can mean ‘the body’ alone. This
is because, apart from other reasons, the <span class="t1 hoverable">use</span> of the plural ‘sarva-kshetreshu’ <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">would</span> have
to be <span class="t2 t5 t11 t18 t19 t23 t26 hoverable">taken</span> as ‘many worlds/creations’ which <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">would</span> be absurd. Also, that the mahAbhUtani ahankAra etc. which the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> explains as kshetram will have to be conceived as
also being multiple, which is also absurd.)
The wording of this verse:
natv evāhaṃ jātu nāsaṃ na tvaṃ neme janādhipāḥ
na caiva na bhaviṣyāmaḥ sarve vayam ataḥ param 2.12
could give an impression that the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> is differentiating Himself from the others and
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">therefore</span> there is duality as taught by the Lord. That such is not the <span class="t5 t16 t21 t24 t25 hoverable">case</span> can be known
from other utterances of the Lord. He says in the 4th chapter:
bahUni mey vyatItAni janmAni tava cha arjuna 4.5
The <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> refers to His present incarnation as a janma of His and Arjuna’s present <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">body</span> as
his janma. It is based on these different bodies that the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> says in the above <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">verse</span> 2.12
that gives the impression mentioned above. That this has to be so is clearly understood
when we see the Lord’s words:
Na jaayate mriyate vaa kadAchit…..2.20 : The Self is never born…..And with regard to
Himself He says: ajopi san avyayAtmA in 4.6.
The <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> also says in 13.16: avibhaktam cha bhUteShu vibhaktam iva cha sthitam:
The One undivisible <span class="t0 t1 t13 t16 t24 t25 hoverable">Consciousness</span> indwells the various bodies and appears as <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">though</span>
divided. This <span class="t0 t1 t13 t16 t24 t25 hoverable">Consciousness</span> is the SharIri, the Kshetrajna indwelling all the bodies.
The plural <span class="t0 t12 hoverable">used</span> in <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">verse</span> 2.12 and the expression: ataḥ param (hereafter) are significant.
There will be transmigration for the jiva-s after death. And Ishwara will not have total
extinction; He will have to be there in every creation. So, in the realm of bondage, plural
has to be spoken of. But this is not the absolute <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">truth</span> is what is shown in this analysis.
Where does the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> teach that there is no plurality in the absolute plane?

23
In the 18th Chapter, for instance, while specifying what constitutes saattvic jnAnam He
says:
sarvabhUteShu yena ekam bhAvam avyayam IkShate
avibhaktam vibhakteShu taj jnAnam viddhi sAttvikam 18.20
The One undiminishing, ever-existing, undifferentiated essence that runs through all the
variety in <span class="t0 t1 t5 t7 t9 t11 t12 t13 t16 t17 t20 t23 t24 t26 t27 t29 hoverable">creation</span> is to be recognized and this constitutes saattvikam jnAnam. The
scriptures point out that this is none other than Brahman. The <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> points out what does
not constitute <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">true</span> knowledge:
pRthaktvena tu yaj jnAnam nAnAbhAvAn pRthagvidhAn
vetti sarveShu bhUteShu taj jnAnam viddhi rAjasam 18.21
Holding that the varied <span class="t0 t1 t15 t22 t25 t29 hoverable">beings</span> are truly different from each other and are distinct entities
is tainted knowledge. Quite contrary to the unenquired notion held by thosee uninitiated
into Shastra that the <span class="t0 t1 t15 t22 t25 t29 hoverable">beings</span> are really different, tattvato bhinnAH, the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> teaches that
the scriptural <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Truth</span> is that the <span class="t0 t1 t15 t22 t25 t29 hoverable">beings</span> are non-different: tattvato abhinnAH.
Where else do we <span class="t5 t14 t15 t24 t27 hoverable">find</span> this teaching in the Gita?
In the 5th Ch. verse,
vidyāvinayasaṃpanne brāhmaṇe gavi hastini
śuni caiva śvapāke ca paṇḍitāḥ samadarśinaḥ 5.18
ihaiva tair jitaḥ sargo yeṣāṃ sāmye sthitaṃ manaḥ
nirdoṣaṃ hi samaṃ brahma tasmād brahmaṇi te sthitāḥ 5.19
In these verses, while teaching the experience of a Jivanmukta, the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> specifies the
Non-dual Atman experience that the Jnani secures and how he <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">would</span> <span class="t25 hoverable">view</span> the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">world</span> of
apparent duality/variety. The Non-dual <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Truth</span> is Samam, of equal nature, in all apparently
different beings. While the Samam is the unchanging essence, the ‘containers’ of this
Samam are ephemeral. They are insubstantial, being products of prakriti. It is the
separating of the Purusha from Prakriti (as taught in the 13th ch.) that constitutes
liberating knowledge. Such a Jnani transcends samsara ‘here itself’ as the above <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">verse</span>
shows and is a mukta.
Again, in this following <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">verse</span> too the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> teaches that the difference among <span class="t0 t1 t15 t22 t25 t29 hoverable">beings</span> is
only seeming and not real:
avibhaktaṃ ca bhūteṣu vibhaktam iva ca sthitam 13.17
The One Indwelling <span class="t0 t1 t13 t16 t24 t25 hoverable">Consciousness</span> remains undivided really but is mistaken to be
differentiated. The variety in the bodies is mistaken to be the variety in the One
Consciousness, Brahman. The word/particle ‘iva’ above shows this.

24
A study of the following seminal <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">verse</span> of the Gita too <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">would</span> prove that the Absolute
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Truth</span> can be only One, Advaitam:
nāsato vidyate bhāvo nābhāvo vidyate sataḥ
ubhayor api dṛṣṭo.antas tv anayos tattvadarśibhiḥ 2.16
Here the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> teaches that the Sat, (that which is seen as ‘ekam BhAvam’ in the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">verse</span>
18.20), is the One inhering principle in all the perishable bodies. The bodies themselves
are asat. The teaching is: There is no existence for the ‘asat’ in all periods of time. And
there is no non-existence of Sat in all periods of time. Sat can be only one; there is no
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">way</span> we can have a variety in Sat. There can be any <span class="t8 t21 t27 hoverable">number</span> of manifestations of Sat, but
Sat in its absolute <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">nature</span> can be One only. Sat is Brahman. Saattvic Jnanam as per the
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> constitutes in apprehending the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Truth</span> as One Sat; a multiplicity is not the right <span class="t23 hoverable">kind</span>
of realization.
All this goes to show that: the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> is not differentiating between Him and others and
also between others from the absolute standpoint. ]

natv evāhaṃ jātu nāsaṃ na tvaṃ neme janādhipāḥ
na caiva na bhaviṣyāmaḥ sarve vayam ataḥ param 2.12
mamaivāṃśo jīvaloke jīvabhūtaḥ sanātanaḥ
manaḥṣaṣṭhānīndriyāṇi prakṛtisthāni karṣati 15.7
The explanation given above applies to the interpreting of these <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">two</span> verses as well. The
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">would</span> not be contradicting the Aupanishadic position about the jiva-jiva bheda. In
the Kathopanishad too there is the mantra similar sounding to the Gita 13.16 we saw
above. It says that it is ‘mahAntam vibhum Atmaanam…’. That which is MahAn and
vibhu cannot be many in number; we cannot have more than one infinite. In the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">light</span> of
these, obviously, the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> in the above <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">two</span> verses is having in <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">mind</span> the multiple
