bodies/minds that is generally experienced in vyavahara. Also that, in <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">order</span> to explain
transmigration to other lokas, rebirth, karma, etc. the difference among jivas is
acknowledged by the Shruti. But this is only in the relative plane. When it comes to
understanding the Tattva that leads to moksha, this relative plane has to be transcended.
The Turiya is taught as ‘shAntam shivam advaitam’. The transcendtal <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Truth</span> does not
transmigrate and has no karma. What transmigrates is only the antaHkarana along with its
samskaras. This is only aupAdhika. The Atman <span class="t1 t8 hoverable">free</span> of these upAdhis is the Atman to be
realized for liberation.
Says the Gita:
sarvabhūteṣu yenaikaṃ bhāvam avyayam īkṣate
avibhaktaṃ vibhakteṣu taj jñānaṃ viddhi sāttvikam 18.20

25
That vision is conducive to liberation which consists of recognizing a Unitary Principle
that runs through the entire creation. A vision that admits absolute differences is
censured by the Gita as rajasic and tamasic.

What about the difference between chetana (sentient) and inert objects?
The general thinking is: We, the perceivers, are chetana, sentient beings, and the
perceived objects are inert, jaDa. In the 13th ch. beginning itself, the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> makes this
distinction: the kshetram, body-mind, jaDa, is the vedya, perceived. The Kshetrajna, the
knower is chaitanya, Consciousness. It <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">would</span> be helpful to know that the kshetram is
otherwise known as prakriti. The similarity between the constituents of the kshetram
spoken of in the 13th ch. and the constituents of prakriti in the 7th ch. is striking. From
the overall teaching of the scriptures, the Gita in particular, we understand that the
prakriti/kshetram is conducive to bondage and liberation consists of separating the
Purusha/Kshetrajna from it. Since liberating <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">knowledge</span> consists of excluding the prakriti
from Purusha, it follows that prakriti is not of the status of the absolutely real; it enjoys
only a relative reality. That which is not absolutely real and is only relatively real is
otherwise <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">called</span> mithya. Now, since we are concerned with the ‘difference between
<span class="t0 t1 t13 t16 t24 t25 hoverable">Consciousness</span> and the kshetram, the jaDa,’ we have to recognize that any difference
(bheda)/relationship (sambandha) between <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">two</span> entities is possible only when they enjoy
the same status of reality. We cannot compare a table in the waking with a table in the
dream. Since the kshetram, jaDa, is accorded the status of ‘mithya’, to say that it is
different from chetana is <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">without</span> any <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t10 t12 t13 t14 t15 t17 t20 t21 t23 t24 t25 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">meaning</span> and substance. There are no ‘two’ entities
to compare and contrast; there is only one chetana and the other cannot be counted along
with the chetana as a second. So, the question of establishing a ‘bheda’ between chetana
and jaDa does not arise at all.
The Chandogya Upanishat Ch.VI teaches:
//vAchArambhanam vikAro nAmadheyam, mRttiketyeva satyam.//
Brahman, Sat, is the material cause that inheres in every <span class="t24 t25 hoverable">object</span> <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">without</span> exception. As
every <span class="t24 t25 hoverable">object</span> is essentially ‘Sat’, the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">truth</span> of every <span class="t24 t25 hoverable">object</span> is ‘Sat’, Brahman. As the
Upanishad teaches the effect is no more than a name, the ‘vastu’ that is seen as an effect
is none other than Sat, Brahman. The ultimate teaching is: Since all objects are
appearances in Brahman, their material cause, they are non-different, abheda, from their
substratum. As such, there is no question of bheda between the Chaityanyam, Brahman,
and the achetana, jada objects.
That the Upanishad teaches that ‘the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">knowledge</span> of the upadana karanam is the one that
makes all the effects, sarvam kAryam, known’ is undisputable. Supposing we <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">take</span> that
the Upanihad is teaching that with the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">knowledge</span> of the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> as the nimittakAranam, an
efficient cause, all else becomes known. This proposal is defective because, everywhere
the karyam, effect, is known on the basis of its upadana karanam, the substance.
Supposing it is said: In the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">world</span> there are many <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">things</span> that are popularly known after

26
their maker, the efficient cause. For example, paintings by Raja Ravi Varma, Picasso or
Da Vinci are famous only by the painter/artiste’s name and not by the material of canvas
or paint <span class="t0 t12 hoverable">used</span> therein. While this is not objected, when we see the example given by the
Chandogya Shruti we come to the firm conclusion that it is not the efficient cause that is
spoken of. The Shruti vakyam is: ekena mritpindena vijnAtena sarvam mrinmayam
vijnAtam syAt…, etc. When the material cause of one product of mud is known, all the
mud-products become known. In the <span class="t5 t16 t21 t24 t25 hoverable">case</span> of the painter/painting we cannot hold this rule
to be true. This is because, it is accepted by all that all (sarvam) the paintings of the past,
present and future universally are not the <span class="t0 t1 t4 t5 t7 t10 t11 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t21 t23 t24 t25 t26 t28 t29 hoverable">works</span> of Ravi Varma, Picasso or Da Vinci or
any single individual. Contrary to this, in the <span class="t5 t16 t21 t24 t25 hoverable">case</span> of the material cause of an earthen pot
universally, at all times, it is mud alone. Further, the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">word</span> ‘mRNmayam’ has the suffix
‘mayat’ which gives the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t10 t12 t13 t14 t15 t17 t20 t21 t23 t24 t25 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">meaning</span> of either vikaara, modification, or prAchurya,
predominance. Both ways, it is the material cause that fits as the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t10 t12 t13 t14 t15 t17 t20 t21 t23 t24 t25 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">meaning</span> of mayat.
What is clinching in the Upanishad is the expression: ‘mRttiketyeva satyam’ [as mud
alone (the mud-products) are real.] This shows beyond doubt that the Upanishad is
talking about the material cause and not the efficient cause, for, it does not say: ‘kulAla
ityeva satyam.’ [‘as potter alone the mud-products are real’]. When an effect is examined,
the maker is not discernible but the material is what is available as inhering in it. Also
that it is not the intention of the Shruti to teach that there is a maker of the universe and
that he is to be known. The drishtAnta <span class="t0 t12 hoverable">used</span> by the Shruti is not needed at all to teach this
well-known <span class="t7 t12 t13 hoverable">fact</span> that every <span class="t24 t25 hoverable">object</span> invariably has a maker. This already well-known <span class="t7 t12 t13 hoverable">fact</span>
does not constitute ‘vijnaanam’. That makes it clear that the Upanishad is talking about
the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">knowledge</span> of the material cause, Brahman, as the vijnanam required togain the
vijnanam pertaining to everything in the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">world</span> If this is not admitted, we will have to
concede that the Upanishad is giving unsuitable, defective examples to teach the Truth.
In the Srimadbhagavatam there is a <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">verse</span> that teaches that the effect is to be viewed as
non-different from its material cause:
kArya-kAraNa-vastvaikya-darshanam paTa-tantu-vat |
avastutvAd-vikalpasya bhAvAdvaitam taduchyate || VII.15.63|| (Prahlada charitram)
[To <span class="t25 hoverable">view</span> the cause-effect as one non-different entity, as in the <span class="t5 t16 t21 t24 t25 hoverable">case</span> of yarn and the cloth
woven with it constitutes bhAvAdvaitam. This is because ‘difference’ (between the
material cause and its effect) is not real.]
The Chandogya Upanishad teaching of ‘vAchArambhanam vikaaro nAmadheyam,
mRttiketyeva satyam’ is what is reflected in the above verse.

To hold <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> as the nimitta kAranam alone also is not <span class="t1 t8 hoverable">free</span> from defect/s. The Shruti
says <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> is ‘nishkriyam’. <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> has no modification <span class="t9 t24 hoverable">born</span> out of action. If it is
said that ‘icchAmAtram’, by mere will, <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> creates the world, then also there is
problem. The Mundaka Shruti says <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> is ‘aprANo hi amanAH shubhraH’. IcchA
is the characteristic of the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">mind</span> and <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> is sans mind. Even to hold <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> as the
material cause will not be strictly correct for He is avikAri; espousing an effect involves

27
modification in the cause. The only <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">way</span> to surmount these problems is to admit that
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> remains Itself unchanging, immutable, by being the adhishthAnam of the
world- appearance. It is only in this <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">way</span> <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> can be the nimitta and upAdAna
jagatkAranam and <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">yet</span> be Nishkriyam, nirvikAri, amanaaH. It is here that the role of
Maya is admitted. To appreciate this, the dream analogy could be considered:
In a dream, I <span class="t5 t14 t15 t24 t27 hoverable">find</span> myself traveling in a bus in a <span class="t0 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t13 t14 t15 t16 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t25 t26 t27 t29 hoverable">city</span> Y; my real <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">place</span> of residence being
<span class="t0 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t13 t14 t15 t16 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t25 t26 t27 t29 hoverable">city</span> X. In the bus, I converse with the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">man</span> seated beside me about the various landmarks
that I see as we move on. I witness several events outside the bus: a funeral procession,
a brawl, a minor accident, etc. The dream part is now over.
Now, analyzing the dream, have I undergone any modification by actually traveling to
the <span class="t0 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t13 t14 t15 t16 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t25 t26 t27 t29 hoverable">city</span> Y, boarding a bus and riding through that city? Obviously no; I have been lying
on my bed in <span class="t0 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t13 t14 t15 t16 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t25 t26 t27 t29 hoverable">city</span> X. Did I make a sankalpa to witness all those <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">things</span> in the dream prior
to the commencement of the dream? No. It just happened by itself. The <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">power</span> of sleep,
nidrAshakti, has conjured up the dream for me to witness. So, I am not the creator really
and I have not undergone any modification in <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">order</span> to create the dream scenes. Could
the nidrAshakti do the dream-creation all by itself? No, this is also not possible; it has to
happen only with my, a Conscious being’s, presence, although passive.
What we saw above is this: <span class="t0 t1 t5 t7 t9 t11 t12 t13 t16 t17 t20 t23 t24 t26 t27 t29 hoverable">Creation</span> requires a shakti. This shakti cannot operate by
itself. It has to depend <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">upon</span> Consciousness. This <span class="t0 t1 t13 t16 t24 t25 hoverable">Consciousness</span> is nirvikAri, nishkriya.
Despite the <span class="t0 t1 t13 t16 t24 t25 hoverable">Consciousness</span> remaining passive, the shakti succeeds in creating a <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t29 hoverable">whole</span>
gamut of experiences. This consisted of creating a ‘me’ with a body-mind with which I
effortlessly identify myself. And the various relationships with a variety of persons,
events, objects, etc. that ‘I’ enter into and sustain. When I have woken up from the
dream I recall, quite justifiably: I saw myself as me, the others, time, space, etc. in the
dream. This is what is <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">called</span> the ‘vivarta’ of <span class="t0 t1 t13 t16 t24 t25 hoverable">Consciousness</span> as all the things/events that
appeared. This appearance could not have come up and existed and ended <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">without</span> me,
the Conscious being lying on the bed. What is the <span class="t23 hoverable">kind</span> of ‘role’ that I have played in
dream-creation? If at all there is a ‘role’ assignable to me, it is only a passive one; I have
just remained stay-put on the bed. My <span class="t0 t1 t13 t16 t24 t25 hoverable">Consciousness</span> was utilized by the shakti and the
dream-creation was projected. At best, my role has been that of a witness.
To apply the analogy to the jagat srishti: <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> is the vivarta upAdaana kArana of the
jagat. No modification takes <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">place</span> in <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> as a result of creation. Yet, the <span class="t0 t1 t5 t7 t9 t11 t12 t13 t16 t17 t20 t23 t24 t26 t27 t29 hoverable">creation</span>
could not be <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">without</span> <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> as its basis. The Shakti that brings forth and sustains the
<span class="t0 t1 t5 t7 t9 t11 t12 t13 t16 t17 t20 t23 t24 t26 t27 t29 hoverable">creation</span> has no existence independent of Brahman, the Chit. <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> the Chit is the
adhishthAnam of the entire jagat and the shakti. The ‘role’ of <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> in the jagat-srishti
is a passive one; It is just a sAkshi, witness. Saakshitvam can be understood as:
akartrutve sati bodhrtvam, ‘knowing sans acting’. This is what is spelt out by Bhagavan
in the Gita (IX.10): mayA adhyakshena prakritiH sUyate charaachram jagat, with Me as
a Witness, Prakriti brings forth the creation. Bhagavan makes His ‘role’ clear by denying
any kartritvam for Himself in creation: tasya kartAram api mAm viddhi akartAram
avyayam, na mey asti kartavyam, svabhAvastu pravartate, etc. His role is mere
adhyakshatvam, SAkshi. This conveys the Vedantic position of: 1. A Nishkriyam

28
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> as an indispensable element in creation, 2. This <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> is a mere witness, 3.
Therefore, Consciousness, 4.The ‘doing’ part is that of Prakriti, 5. All these mean that
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> is not really ‘nimitta kAranam’, efficient cause, of the creation, prakriti, being
the one undergoing modification, is the pariNAmi upAdAna kaaranam, and <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> is
just the vivarta upAdAna kAranam of creation, 6. The final Vedantic position is: The
<span class="t0 t1 t5 t7 t9 t11 t12 t13 t16 t17 t20 t23 t24 t26 t27 t29 hoverable">creation</span> is merely an appearance of <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> as the chara-acharam jagat through the
instrumentality/intervention/modification of Prakriti, Maaya. That is why we <span class="t5 t14 t15 t24 t27 hoverable">find</span>
expressions like: Maayaa nirmitam jagat, Brahma kAryam jagat, etc. being variously
<span class="t0 t12 hoverable">used</span> in Vedantic works. While understanding these statements we have to keep in mind:
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> is vivarta upAdaanam, MAyA is parinAmi upaadAnam and the jagat is an
appearance of <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> just as a bangle, chain and ring are appearances of gold.
Brahman, the Sat, Chit, <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">without</span> which prakriti cannot create, remains as It is. He who
realizes himself as <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> is Amrta, ShAshvata, Sanaatana. For, the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">nature</span> of Sat is: na
abhAvo vidyate SataH [Existence will never go out of existence] (Gita II.16) and the
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">nature</span> of Chit is: na hi drashTurdRshTer viparilopo vidyate, avinAshitvAt [the vision that
is <span class="t0 t1 t13 t16 t24 t25 hoverable">Consciousness</span> of the seer is never lost, for It is Imperishable](Brhadaaranyaka Up
IV.iii.25)
[An aside point: Shakti or Maya is anAdi and is an upAdhi of Brahman. It is
unreasonable to look for a cause of what is admitted as anAdi; ‘Prakritim purusham
chaiva viddhyanAdI ubhAvapi’ says the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> in the Gita. This is <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">called</span> ‘avidyopAdhi’
and owing to this UpAdhi-sambandha all the effects, aupAdhika, emerge. Why is Maya
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">called</span> an upAdhi? It is because in its ‘presence’ <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> is seen, mistakenly, as creator,
etc. For example, a crystal, in the proximate presence of a red flower, appears as red; the
red flower/redness is the upaadhi. When SvarUpa jnanam dawns it destroys this upAdhisambandha (chidachitgranthi) as <span class="t0 t1 t3 t4 t5 t6 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">well</span> as the upadhi itself (as <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> is taught by the
Shastra and realized by the sadhaka as advitIyam satya vastu and Maya is mithya) and
shows forth <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> as <span class="t1 t8 hoverable">free</span> from the upAdhi. The jagat is rendered ‘baadhita’, sublated,
since <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> has been ‘separated’ from Maya.]
When <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> is spoken of as the abhinna-nimitta-upAdAna-kAranam of jagat, it is
only by ‘associating’ Maya with Brahman. This is the principle of Ishwara who is the
subject matter, in the cosmic level, of the <span class="t26 hoverable">third</span> pAda of the Mandukya Upanishat (6th
mantra). He is spoken of as antaryAmI, SarveshwaraH, the jagad yOni, etc. The
<span class="t0 t1 t13 t16 t24 t25 hoverable">Consciousness</span> bereft of this ‘association’ with Maya is taught as the TurIya, Atman,
Advaitam in the chaturtha pAda of this Upanishat. It is the realization of the Turiya
Atman that is termed ‘vijnAnam’ resulting in Moksha.
We see in the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">world</span> that every <span class="t24 t25 hoverable">object</span> is known through the main material that goes into
its making. For example, we say: suvarnAtmakam kundalam, a golden earring,
mrdAtmakaH ghataH, an earthen pot, etc. We do not encounter expressions like:
kulAlAtmakaH sharaavaH, a potter-pot, pAchakAtmakaH soopaH, cook/chef-soup, etc.
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Thus</span> the Upanishadic Teaching is: Brahma/SadAtmakam jagat, where the substance of
the kArya-jagat is none other than Sat; the nama-rupa aspect of the jagat is insubstantial –

29
vAchArambhanam vikAro nAmadheyam. Sat is Brahman, Sat is Atma. So teaches the
Mahavakya: Tat tvam asi.
In the context of discussing the upAdaana-kAranatva, material causehood, of <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> it
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">would</span> be helpful to refer to the <span class="t8 t21 t27 hoverable">number</span> of instances in the Gita where the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> says He is
the ‘Bijam’ (seed), ‘pitA’ (Father), the Source of origin, sustenance and resolution of the
universe, etc. The Mandukya Upanishad (6) refers to Brahman/Ishwara as the ‘Yoni’
(womb) of the universe. These are references to the material-causehood of
Brahman/Ishwara. A mere efficient/intelligent cause like a painter or a potter or a
goldsmith is not seen in the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">world</span> to provide the essential ‘seed’ in the products that are
made. Certainly these makers are not the yoni, womb, of the products. The Brahmasutras
‘prakRtishcha …..’ (I.iv.23), ‘yonishcha hi gIyate’ (I.iv.27) teach that the Supreme is the
material cause of the universe. There are a <span class="t8 t21 t27 hoverable">number</span> of Shruti passages that talk of the
material causehood of Brahman. For example, ‘kartAram Isham Purusham Brahma
yonim (Mundaka Up. 3.1.3), ‘yad bhUtayonim paripashyanti dhIrAH’ (Mundaka 1.1.6),
the Kaivalyopanishad ‘UmA-sahaayam Parameshwaram…..bhUtayonim…tamasaH
parastAt’ teach this same idea. The PANini Sutra (I.iv.30) ‘janikartuH prakRtiH’ teaches
that the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">word</span> ‘prakRtiH’ means progenitor. There is nothing wrong in referring to the
PANini Sutra as VyAkaraNa is a valid VedAnga which aids in determining the purport of
the Veda. The lexicon ‘Amara kosha’ III.2480 says: ‘prakRtir-yoni-linge’. The
commentary thereon says: ‘yonau linge cha prakRtiH’.
Are the various insentient objects not different mutually?
Having seen that the chetana (Ishvara/jiva) - jaDa bheda is untenable in absolute terms,
we may now examine the position that the jaDa padarthas are mutually different. The
Gita says:
na tad asti pṛthivyāṃ vā divi deveṣu vā punaḥ
sattvaṃ prakṛtijair muktaṃ yad ebhiḥ syāt tribhir guṇaiḥ 18.40
The entire category <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">called</span> ‘objects’, jaDa, kshetram, can be grouped under one name:
prakriti. The above <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">verse</span> says that there is no <span class="t24 t25 hoverable">object</span> in all the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">three</span> worlds that is bereft
of the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">three</span> gunas <span class="t9 t24 hoverable">born</span> of prakriti/maya. The objects are different in their name, form,
utility, etc. But in essence, they are not different from each other. What is the essence
that is the unifying factor? It is the material cause of the objects/kshetram which is the
sattva-rajas-tamo-gunAtmikA mAyaa. In the manifest states of the waking and dream we
observe the variety in objects. In the <span class="t0 t1 t10 t14 t21 t23 t25 t29 hoverable">state</span> of sleep, all the objects resolve into their
cause, the undifferentiated state. Thus, it is not possible to establish any real bheda
between one jada <span class="t24 t25 hoverable">object</span> and another. All differences pertain to names/forms/utility, etc.
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Yet</span> another categorization of the entire gamut of the objective <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">world</span> is: shabda, sparsha,
rasa, etc. All the objects come under this five-fold category. This itself resolves into the
pancha-bhUtas that are the cause of the objects. The pancha-bhutas are again evolutes of
Maya. Thus, as the kArana prakriti, no kArya-vastu, object, is essentially different from
another.
The concept of abheda is possible in the realm of the jaDa prapancha as also in the

30
Chaitanyam. All bodies are a product of food, annam. On this basis there is no
difference between one <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">body</span> and another. The indwelling <span class="t0 t1 t13 t16 t24 t25 hoverable">Consciousness</span> in every <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">body</span>
is also the same and no difference can be spoken of on that basis too. The dravya <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">called</span>
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">mind</span> in each being is also the same; manas being a product of the sattvaguna-samashti of
the pancha bhUtas which are again the evolutes of prakriti. Any difference is possible
only in the realm of nama-rUpa which is again taught by the Chandogya Shruti to be only
word-based and not substantial. The substance of everything in <span class="t0 t1 t5 t7 t9 t11 t12 t13 t16 t17 t20 t23 t24 t26 t27 t29 hoverable">creation</span> is ultimately
Brahman, Sat.
The essence of the consideration of the five’bhedas’(jIva-Ishvara bheda, jiva-jiva bheda,
jiva-jaDa bheda, Ishwara-jaDa bheda and jada-jada bheda) is contained in an
encapsulated <span class="t0 t1 t2 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">form</span> in the 7th mantra of the Mandukya Upanishat: ‘nAntaH prajnam….’
All duality is categorically negated as pertaining to the relatively real (mithya) realm, the
pAda-traya, and the Turiya is declared as the Absolute Truth: Advaitam Atma.
The Panchadashi, Chitra Deepa Prakaranam (Ch.VI) teaches the method of
comprehending the Non-dual Brahman/Atman by taking the example of a painting on a
cloth/canvas. We can show that the five bheda-s (considered above) are not real in the
absolute <span class="t0 t1 t7 t12 t13 t14 t17 t23 t27 t28 hoverable">sense</span> by studying this example. Let us suppose we have a painting-on-canvas of
a scene of a market place. There are various people, <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">men</span> and women, different animals
like cows, dogs, sheep, etc., several birds like crows, pigeons and so on depicted in the
painting. There are many insentient objects like dress materials, <span class="t0 t14 t23 t24 hoverable">food</span> grains, sweet-meats,
soft drinks, etc. that are being sold there. There is a temple and <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">people</span> go in and come
out of it.
What is fundamental to the above example is: the wide variety of sentient and insentient
entities is having one common base, the canvas. Although the outlines, the colour, the
presence of clothing on the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">people</span> and its absence on animals, cars, cycles, etc. differ, the
entire ‘difference’ stands on the one substratum, the canvas. The five bheda-s are
observable only on the surface but when the substratum canvas is considered, the bheda-s
no longer matter. The shopkeeper-customer (jiva-jiva) difference, the shopkeeperfoodgrain (jiva-jaDa) difference, the temple Deity-devotee (Ishwara-jiva) difference, the
food-grain-cycle (jaDa-jaDa) difference, temple Deity-temple bell (Ishwara-jaDa)
difference are all perceived only apparently but fade into insignificance the moment it is
realized that the entire gamut of variety stands on one common substratum, the canvas. It
is to be noted that the variety of objects, sentient and insentient, has no existence apart
from the canvas on which they are painted. The objects cannot be ‘separated’ from the
canvas.
The canvas is the One Non-dual Consciousness, the Sat, Chit, Ananta Brahman/Atman,
the drk. The variety, drishya, is only a superimposition on this substratum. The variety
has no existence apart from the <span class="t0 t1 t13 t16 t24 t25 hoverable">Consciousness</span> on which it appears.
The consideration of a dream, as an analogy, also <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">would</span> <span class="t3 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t12 t13 t17 t18 t19 t20 t22 t23 t27 t29 hoverable">bring</span> out the same results as
above. The Shruti says: na iha nAnaa asti kinchana (No difference whatsoever exists
here in Brahman).

31
The five bheda-s were <span class="t2 t5 t11 t18 t19 t23 t26 hoverable">taken</span> up for consideration not <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">without</span> a purpose. All bheda,
duality, forms the subject matter of aparaa vidyaa, the sciences that pertain to the world.
The Veda too has this portion when it teaches the purusharthas of dharma, artha and
kAma. But when it comes to Moksha, the vidya takes the name of ‘parA vidyA’. This
field of the Shastra is essentially the one that transcends bheda, duality. The main
purport and purpose of the Vedanta, the Upanishads, is to teach abheda and only in this
the Upanishads become the indispensable pramana. While bheda, duality, is perceived
naturally, <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">without</span> being instructed, abheda is not; it requires to be instructed with effort
and understood with <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">great</span> effort. It is towards this end the Upanishads endeavour. Says
Sri Shankara Bhagavatpada in His commentary to the mantra 5.1.1 of the Brihararanyaka
Upanishad:
//na upadeshArham dvaitam, jAta-mAtra-prAni-buddhi-gamyatvAt.//
[Duality does not require to be instructed (by the Veda) since it (duality) is perceived by
every being even at birth.]
A question <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">would</span> arise: If this is the case, why does the Veda <span class="t6 t9 t11 t19 t20 t22 hoverable">speak</span> of duality in <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">great</span>
volumes? Reply: The Veda is actually refining the duality that is initially crude by
making it conducive to the grasping of the ultimate teaching of Advaitam. All kinds of
duality like: he is different and I am different, I am his/her son/daughter, I am dependent
on him/her for my sustenance/wellbeing, etc. is cognized by every being even untutored.
Even a just <span class="t9 t24 hoverable">born</span> baby or pup or calf looks <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">upon</span> the mother for being fed and security.
This dependence on an external source continues as the child grows up. It looks up to the
teacher for knowledge. The grown up <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">man</span> looks <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">upon</span> the employer, sva-svAmi-bhAva,
for monetary benefits and to lead a <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">life</span> of happiness. The Veda takes this forward and
teaches us that we have to look <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">upon</span> Ishwara for our wellbeing. It teaches us the
existence of other worlds and helps us in attaining these by adhering to the means
prescribed therein. It teaches us that the karmaphala dhAta is Ishwara and He is the One
that can grant us the Parama PurushArtha, Moksha. All this is the refinement the Veda
does in the realm of duality. It is only when it comes to the instruction pertaining to
Moksha, the Veda takes a quantum jump, as witnessed in the Mandukya 7th mantra, and
negates all duality, totally and holds out the Advaitic <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Truth</span> as the means for Moksha
which itself is ShAntam, Shivam, Advaitam.
The pitiable status of the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">world</span>
The analysis conducted above gives rise to a situation where the status of the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">world</span> is in
question. The <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> says in the Bhagavadgita:
mayā tatam idaṃ sarvaṃ jagad avyaktamūrtinā
matsthāni sarvabhūtāni na cāhaṃ teṣv avasthitaḥ 9.4
na ca matsthāni bhūtāni paśya me yogam aiśvaram
bhūtabhṛn na ca bhūtastho mamātmā bhūtabhāvanaḥ 9.5

32
In the first half of the first verse, the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> says that He, Brahman, pervades the entire
world. The Gita says elsewhere that there is no <span class="t24 t25 hoverable">object</span> in all the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">three</span> worlds that is not a
product of prakriti. Prakriti is the other name for kshetram, the observed world. It is
inert principle while the Atman, the kshetrajna, the Purusha, is Consciousness. When it is
said that <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> pervades the entire world, what is meant is: the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">world</span> has no
existence/shine of its own apart from that of Brahman. This dependence of the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">world</span> on
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> is what is said in the <span class="t26 hoverable">third</span> quarter of the first verse: ‘the <span class="t0 t1 t15 t22 t25 t29 hoverable">beings</span> (world) rest(s)
in Me’
In the fourth quarter of the first <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">verse</span> the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> states that He, Brahman, does not inhere in
this world. He hastens to add, in the next verse, that nor does the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">world</span> inhere in Him.
What results from these statements of the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> is: The <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">world</span> is neither established in
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> nor does <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> support the world. This leaves the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">world</span> <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">without</span> any real
basis. A real supporter-supported relationship is possible only between <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">two</span> finite, saavayava objects. In the present case, <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> is Infinite, niravayava. It is a-sanga and
hence no type of relationship is possible for It with the world. The situation is akin to
the superimposed snake on the substratum of a rope. The rope does not inhere in the
snake as the snake, being illusory, does not have an existence of its own. Nor does the
snake really rest on the rope as the rope in no <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">way</span> supports the illusory snake. Then
where does the snake exist? The only answer to this is: the illusory snake exists only in
the imagination of the one who thinks it exists. Similar is the <span class="t5 t16 t21 t24 t25 hoverable">case</span> with the world. It
exists only in the imagination of the one who believes it exists.
This very teaching is <span class="t1 t3 t4 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t13 t15 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t27 t29 hoverable">brought</span> out by the Veda/Upanishads in several ways:
‘yatra hi dvaitam iva bhavati…..’ ‘mRtyoH sa mRtyum gacchati ya iha nAna iva
pashyati’, ‘vAchArambhaNam vikAro nAmadheyam’, ‘sarvANi rUpANi vichitya
dhIraH nAmAni kRtvA abhivadan…’ By using the particle ‘iva’, the Upanishad says that
the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">world</span> is as <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">though</span> existent but not really.
The above Gita verses also <span class="t3 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t12 t13 t17 t18 t19 t20 t22 t23 t27 t29 hoverable">bring</span> out the vivartopAdana-kAraNatvam of Brahman. This
is akin to the rope being a ‘material cause’ for the appearing snake. The rope has
certainly not provided any of its material to the snake appearance except its existence
which is the foundation <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">upon</span> which the perceiver imagines a snake. The rope only
appears to be a snake for this perceiver. Brahman, by not inhering in the world, does not
lend any real material for the world. <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> is only appearing as the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">world</span> to the one
who perceives the world. This is what is termed as the vivartopAdanatvam of <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span>
in respect of the world. The Chandogya Shruti ‘vAchArambhaNam vikAro
nAmadheyam, mRttiketyeva satyam’ teaches that the various products of clay are mere
appearances of clay; their substance is only clay. In giving this analogy, the Upanishad
teaches that the world, a product of Brahman, is only an appearance of Brahman; its
substance is Brahman. As <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">world</span> it is insubstantial.
ye caiva sātvikā bhāvā rājasās tāmasāś ca ye
matta eveti tān viddhi na tv ahaṃ teṣu te mayi 7.12

33
This <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">verse</span> too could be seen in the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">light</span> of the above explanation.
The jnana-chakshus:
The Gita says:
utkrāmantaṃ sthitaṃ vāpi bhuñjānaṃ vā guṇānvitam
vimūḍhā nānupaśyanti paśyanti jñānacakṣuṣaḥ 15.10
yatanto yoginaś cainaṃ paśyanty ātmany avasthitam
yatantopy akṛtātmāno nainaṃ paśyanty acetasaḥ 15.11
In these couple of verses we can discern the ‘AdhyAsic’ <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">nature</span> of the jivatvopadhi. The
jiva, out of ignorance of his <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">true</span> <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">nature</span> (which is described in the II ch. as ‘ajo nityaH
shaashvato’yam purAnaH etc. which are also the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">true</span> <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">nature</span> applicable to Brahman),
identifies himself with the imagined upadhis <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">called</span> body-mind complex and experiences
the upadhi-dharmas as his own dharmas. <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Thus</span> he says: I am born, I experience sukha
duhkha bhoga, I will grow old, I am subject to disease and finally I will die. I am subject
to rebirth and <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">therefore</span> am a miserable samsari. Bhagavan calls this by the name
‘vimUDha drishti’, the <span class="t25 hoverable">view</span> of the ignorant, deluded. The <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> says: Those who are
ignorantly identifying themselves with all these upadhidharmas are failing to see the
Chaitanyam to whom these are seemingly happening. It is only he who possesses the
jnana-chakshus <span class="t9 t24 hoverable">born</span> out of shashtra-acharya upadesha and sadhana can separate the
Chaitanyam, Atman, from these upadhis and become freed of samsara. The <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> says in
the 13th ch. PurushaH prakritistho hi bhunkte prakritjAn guNAn. This is akin to the
seeing of the snake in the rope (vimUdha drishti) and later knowing the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Truth</span> by
applying the appropriate pramana: jnana-chakshus. Here the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> is teaching the
Adhyasic <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">nature</span> of the samsaric experience. This is what is elaborately <span class="t1 t3 t4 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t13 t15 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t27 t29 hoverable">brought</span> out by
the Bhashyakara in the Adhyasa Bhashya. The ‘adhyAsa Bhashya’ contains an analogy:
ekashchandraH sa-dvitIyavad, ‘the really only one moon appearing as <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">though</span> <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">two</span> in
number’. The <span class="t5 t16 t21 t24 t25 hoverable">case</span> of the ‘two birds’ is similar to this and the Mundaka Shruti is alluding
to this common error on the part of the deluded jivas by initially ‘approving’ it and later
correcting the vision.
Now, looking at the above quoted <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">verse</span> once again, we get this insight: The dvitIyA
vibhakti, accusative case, in the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">verse</span> 15.10 is of <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">great</span> significance. Supposing the police
is looking for a criminal named Mohan. They know that he is speeding away in a car,
identified by the police. They have an informant with them and are closely following the
criminal’s car. That car contains five others also. Now, the police want to know who
among the five is Mohan so that in <span class="t5 t16 t21 t24 t25 hoverable">case</span> they have to shoot him, they should not be
making a mistake. So, they ask the informant to identify Mohan. The informant looks
into the car and identifies: ‘The one who is driving is Mohan.’
Now, in the present context we have a similar identification made by the Gita. It says:
The one who is seen to be involved in samsara as a kartA-bhoktA, endowed with the
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">three</span> guNas, who is subject to birth, <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">death</span> and transmigration, is Brahman. The dvitIyA

34
vibhakti is significant in this <span class="t0 t1 t7 t12 t13 t14 t17 t23 t27 t28 hoverable">sense</span> of identifying the chaitanyam with jIvatvOpAdhi as
the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> that is to be realized as nirupAdhika chaitanyam. This realization confers
liberation. This is stated in the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">verse</span> 15.11. The <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">words</span> ‘enam’ ‘this one’, and ‘ātmany
avasthitam’ ‘one established in the intellect’ convey the MahAvAkyArtha that the
chaitanyam seen to be endowed with jivatvopAdhi in the earlier <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">verse</span> is the chaitanyam
that is seated in the intellect. That it is Ishwara chaitanyam that is seated in everyone’s
intellect is taught by the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> in this very chapter: sarvasya chAham hRdi
sanniviShTo…I am seated in everyone’s intellect…..
Just as the Police apprehend Mohan for his crime and not for his driving or wearing
denims, the aspirant, by invoking the JnanachakshuH, apprehends the Pure
<span class="t0 t1 t13 t16 t24 t25 hoverable">Consciousness</span> by discarding the jivatopadhi-dharmas which are only incidental and not
svarUpa dharma.
It is gaining this vision that is spoken of as ‘jnAna chakshUs’ by the Gita.

Perception of duality and the Jivanmukta
//The Advaitic concept of a jîvanmukta is also absurd because a <span class="t0 t4 t5 t10 t22 t25 t28 hoverable">person</span> who has
surmounted the realm of perception and realized the Absolute (as Advaita holds of a
mukta) should not continue to exist <span class="t0 t1 t4 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t23 t24 t25 t28 t29 hoverable">within</span> and interact with the realm of perception that
he has realized as being not-Real—no one continues to perceive a snake after realizing
that the <span class="t24 t25 hoverable">object</span> of his perception is actually a rope. The suggestion that such bondage to
the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">world</span> of perception continues for a while after the occurrence of Realization, because
of past attachments, is not tenable—such attachments themselves are artifacts of the
perceived <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">world</span> that has supposedly been sublated, and should not continue to besiege
the <span class="t0 t1 t13 t16 t24 t25 hoverable">consciousness</span> of the Realized. If they do, then we have to either reject the Realization
that is said to have occurred, or else reject the notion that the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">world</span> of perception, as
manifesting through the attachments on a supposedly Realized person, can be sublated. In
either instance, the notion of jîvanmukti is not meaningful. //
Reply: The objection has stemmed out of an improper understanding of the
Vedanta/Advaita prakriya. The analogy of rope-snake is not very appropriate in the <span class="t5 t16 t21 t24 t25 hoverable">case</span>
of jivanmukti. This analogy suits the explanation of the adhyasa and its removal. But
what condition prevails post-adhyasa-removal is not clearly <span class="t1 t3 t4 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t13 t15 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t27 t29 hoverable">brought</span> out by this example.
To explain this state, the other example, employed by the Acharya, of mirage-water is
what is apt. The Acharya has explained this in the Gita(?) bhashyam (ref.) We can <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">take</span>
the example and apply it in the modern context:
Supposing, I am driving on a highway on a summer day. The <span class="t0 t1 t3 t4 t5 t7 t9 t10 t11 t12 t14 t15 t16 t18 t19 t21 t22 t24 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">sun</span> has <span class="t0 t1 t3 t4 t5 t6 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">well</span> risen and in
the noon <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">time</span> there is formation of mirages on the highway ahead of me. Actually there
is no formation of mirage; it is only an appearance of the mirage to me, the perceiver,
from a particular spot and angle. When the spot/angle is changed, the appearance ceases.
Nevertheless, when I maintain the position and angle even while driving, there are
chances that I continue to see mirages as I proceed. At the first instance, if I am new to

35
that locality, I might mistake it for a water-spread, puddle, on the road and might even
exercise caution to avoid any skidding and regulate my speed. But the moment I realize
that it is after all a mirage, I am no longer cautious in that respect. I drive <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">without</span> that
aspect engaging my mind, even <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">though</span> I continue to see mirages almost upto 4 in the
afternoon on the highway.
Similar is the <span class="t5 t16 t21 t24 t25 hoverable">case</span> with the Mukta who has known that the perception-based prapancha is
unreal. By ‘sublation’ what is meant is: the satyatva buddhi of the aropita vastu is
destroyed. It is not necessary that the aropita vastu itself should go out of (perceptual)
existence. If this is not admitted and appreciated there will be problem in explaining
various actions of the Mukta. For example, the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> says that the Tattvadarshi, when
approached in the appropriate manner, will impart the Atmavidya to the jijnasu. If the
Tattvadarshi were to himself become non-existent soon after the dawn of knowledge,
how is valid tattvopadesha possible, as mentioned by the Lord? To carry out the
tattvopadesha, the Mukta (‘Muktashcha anyAn vimochayEt’ is a part of a famous shloka:
durjanassajjano bhUyAt/sajjanH shAntimApnuyAt/shAnto muchyeta
bandhebhyaH/muktashcha anyAn vimochayet//) has to ‘perceive’ the jignasu and see him
as ‘another’, listen to his questions, doubts, etc. and give out the teaching suitably. All
this can happen only if the perception-based <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">world</span> is remaining intact, although for the
Tattvadarshi it is only asatya. The <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> echoes this <span class="t0 hoverable">idea</span> when He says:
yadyad ācarati śreṣṭhas tattad evetaro janaḥ
sa yat pramāṇaṃ kurute lokas tad anuvartate 3.21
na me pārthāsti kartavyaṃ triṣu lokeṣu kiṃcana
nānavāptam avāptavyaṃ varta eva ca karmaṇi 3.22
yadi hy ahaṃ na varteyaṃ jātu karmaṇy atandritaḥ
mama vartmānuvartante manuṣyāḥ pārtha sarvaśaḥ 3.23
Even <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">though</span> the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> has nothing to gain by acting in the world, <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">yet</span> He acts. This is the
<span class="t0 t1 t10 t14 t21 t23 t25 t29 hoverable">state</span> of the Jivanmukta. His <span class="t0 t1 t10 t14 t21 t23 t25 t29 hoverable">state</span> has been voiced by the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> in this very chapter:
yas tv ātmaratir eva syād ātmatṛptaś ca mānavaḥ
ātmany eva ca saṃtuṣṭas tasya kāryaṃ na vidyate 3.17
naiva tasya kṛtenārtho nākṛteneha kaścana
na cāsya sarvabhūteṣu kaścid arthavyapāśrayaḥ 3.18
anAditvAt nirgunatvAt paramAtma ayam avyayaH |
sharIrastho’pi kounteya na karoti na lipyate || (13.31)
Compare the above with the following.
navadvāre pure dehī naiva kurvan na kārayan 5.13

36
{These <span class="t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t20 t22 t24 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">set</span> of verses too teach that the jivanmukta is non-different from Brahman, the
Lord.}
If lokasangraha, tattvopadesha, etc. are to happen, the perceptual <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">world</span> has to exist.
There is no <span class="t1 t11 t16 t20 t25 t27 t28 hoverable">reason</span> for it to be believed to be absolutely real by the tattvadarshi, as in the
<span class="t5 t16 t21 t24 t25 hoverable">case</span> of Bhagavan as well. The mirage can continue to be perceived but that there is no
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">water</span> there is known by the one who has shifted the angle and position and realized the
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">truth</span> but returns to the same angle/position and continues driving. The shift in perception
has <span class="t2 t5 t11 t18 t19 t23 t26 hoverable">taken</span> <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">place</span> in the mind. Although the <span class="t2 t6 t19 t20 t26 t29 hoverable">eyes</span> report <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">water</span> there, the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">mind</span> knows that
there is no <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">water</span> there. Similarly, although the indriyas report the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">world</span> of perception,
the Mukta knows that they are not absolutely true. With this <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">knowledge</span> intact, sthitaa
prajnaa, he lives in the world, nava-dvare pure, naiva kurvan na kArayan, just as the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span>
remains in His sva-Maya-nirmita <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">body</span> and performs actions, even <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">though</span> He is akarta,
aja, avyaya.
That the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> sees the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">world</span> as an adhyAropa, a pratibhAsa, in Him is spelt out by
Himself in the 9th Ch.
mayā tatam idaṃ sarvaṃ jagad avyaktamūrtinā
matsthāni sarvabhūtāni na cāhaṃ teṣv avasthitaḥ 9.4
na ca matsthāni bhūtāni paśya me yogam aiśvaram
bhūtabhṛn na ca bhūtastho mamātmā bhūtabhāvanaḥ 9.5
The Lord’s teaching is: Even <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">though</span> it might appear that the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">world</span> rests in Me, by virtue
of My ‘being its upAdAna KAraNam’, still in <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">truth</span> it does not rest in Me as I, Brahman,
am only the vivartopadAna kAraNam of the world. So, how then does the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> go about
doing His actions? It is with the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">knowledge</span> that the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">world</span> is an appearance that He acts,
since He is akarta in truth. This is the <span class="t0 t1 t10 t14 t21 t23 t25 t29 hoverable">state</span> of the Jivanmukta. He knows that the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">world</span>
is an adhyaropa in the Atman. With this firm <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">knowledge</span> he goes about his vyavahara,
not being bound by his actions. At the same time, the actions of a Jivanmukta, like that
of the Lord, are of immense help to the baddha jivas.
The ‘sublation’ of the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">world</span> of perception for the Tattvavit is spoken of by Bhagavan in
these verses:
naiva kiṃcit karomīti yukto manyeta tattvavit
paśyañ śṛṇvan spṛśañ jighrann aśnan gacchan svapañ śvasan 5.8
pralapan visṛjan gṛhṇann unmiṣan nimiṣann api
indriyāṇīndriyārtheṣu vartanta iti dhārayan 5.9
In the above verses one can see the mention of almost all the activities of the <span class="t0 t1 t7 t12 t13 t14 t17 t23 t27 t28 hoverable">sense</span>
organs. The realm of the activity of the <span class="t0 t1 t7 t12 t13 t14 t17 t23 t27 t28 hoverable">sense</span> organs is the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">world</span> of perception. To the
Tattvavit who knows that he, the Atman/Brahman, is not the pramAtru and <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">therefore</span> not

37
the doer/enjoyer, this <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">world</span> of perception is only a show of the unreal prakriti. This is
because, as taught by the Lord:
prakṛteḥ kriyamāṇāni guṇaiḥ karmāṇi sarvaśaḥ
ahaṃkāravimūḍhātmā kartāham iti manyate 3.27
tattvavit tu mahābāho guṇakarmavibhāgayoḥ
guṇā guṇeṣu vartanta iti matvā na sajjate 3.28
it is the prakriti’s realm which is the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">world</span> of perception. As the Jnani has separated
himself from the realm of prakriti (otherwise <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">called</span> the kshetram), as taught by the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span>
in the 13th chapter:
kṣetrakṣetrajñayor evam antaraṃ jñānacakṣuṣā
bhūtaprakṛtimokṣaṃ ca ye vidur yānti te param 13.35
the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">world</span> of perception is sublated. The activity of ‘eating’, etc., of the Jivanmukta is
quite possible in the manner taught by the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> in the verses 5.8 and 9 above. This is one
of the instances where the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> is teaching Jivanmukti. The Tattvavit, mukta, is with the
firm realization that naiva kiṃcit karomīti yukto manyeta tattvavit (I never perform
these actions). The <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> is talking of these actions for a <span class="t0 t4 t5 t10 t22 t25 t28 hoverable">person</span> who is alive and not to a
one who has departed from the world. The usage of the ‘shatr’ pratyaya in the words:
paśyañ śṛṇvan spṛśañ jighrann aśnan gacchan svapañ śvasan 5.8
pralapan visṛjan gṛhṇann unmiṣan nimiṣann api 5.9 are noteworthy. This pratyaya
indicates a present continuous tense where even when the action is going on, the
realization that one is not the doer is present. The Brihadaranyaka Upanishad (IV.v.15)
gives the larger picture of this <span class="t0 t1 t10 t14 t21 t23 t25 t29 hoverable">state</span> of Jivanmukti which the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> stated in the verses just
seen:

<span class="t0 t1 t10 t14 t21 t23 t25 t29 hoverable">state</span> of ignorance.

The Chandogyopanishat VII.24.1 too states the above after first stating that the <span class="t0 t1 t10 t14 t21 t23 t25 t29 hoverable">state</span> of
ignorance as ‘alpam’. It contrasts the above with the <span class="t0 t1 t10 t14 t21 t23 t25 t29 hoverable">state</span> of jivanmukti as ‘bhUmA’.

The Jivanmukta has realized his <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">true</span> <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">nature</span> as the One Absolute Chaitanyam, the Allpervading Witness of the realm of prakriti, the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">world</span> of perception. This <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">nature</span> of the
Truth/Jivanmukta is taught by the Shvetashvataropanishat in the VI.11 mantra: Eko
devaH sarvabhuteshu gUDhaH…..sAkshI chetaaH kevalo nirgunashcha…:
%pin;t!
ñetañraepin;t!
