@kae dev> svR-Ute;u gUF>
svRVyapI svR-UtaNtraTma,
kmaRXy]> svR-Utaixvas>
sa]I ceta kevlae inguR[í. 11.
Although, from his point of view, the Jivanmukta sees only the Atman/Brahman,
everywhere, <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">yet</span> from the point of <span class="t25 hoverable">view</span> of the baddha jivas, there is something ‘true’
happening to their benefit. The <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> says:
na kartṛtvaṃ na karmāṇi lokasya sṛjati prabhuḥ
na karmaphalasaṃyogaṃ svabhāvas tu pravartate 5.14
nādatte kasyacit pāpaṃ na caiva sukṛtaṃ vibhuḥ
ajñānenāvṛtaṃ jñānaṃ tena muhyanti jantavaḥ 5.15
The <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> places the entire onus of samsara on the avidya of the jiva. The avidya-nivritti
too takes <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">place</span> owing to the seriousness, sincerity, dedication, application, hard work, etc
of the jiva. The role of the Tattvadarshi and the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> is in no <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">way</span> insignificant. It is
Their anugraha, constant goading, teaching, etc. that trigger the seriousness,
mumukshutvam, in the jiva and helps him cross over samsara. <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Without</span> Their being a
‘role model’, the jiva is nowhere in the path of progress.
Supposing, someone does not want to admit jivanmukti. Let us consider the situation of
a Tattvadarshi imparting jnanam to a jijnaasu. The Gita says the Tattvadarshi sees
Atman/Brahman, Bhagavan everywhere and in everything. Now, the Jnani sees This in
the jijnasu too. Since the jijnasu is Brahman/Atman, where is the need to teach him? To
avoid this situation, one will have to say: Although the jijnasu is Brahman/Atman from
the Tattvadarshi’s standpoint, to the jijnasu this <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">truth</span> is not <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">yet</span> aparoksha. So, the Guru
considers him a jijnasu and imparts the teaching. This is exactly the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">way</span> the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> views
the world/people. Although the entire jagat is non-different from the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> (should we not
admit, on the basis of the Lord’s teaching, that the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> too sees Atman/Brahman

39
everywhere and in everything?), <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">yet</span> the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> has chosen to teach by <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">word</span> and by
example.
saktāḥ karmaṇy avidvāṃso yathā kurvanti bhārata
kuryād vidvāṃs tathāsaktaś cikīrṣur lokasaṃgraham 3.25
na buddhibhedaṃ janayed ajñānāṃ karmasaṃginām
joṣayet sarvakarmāṇi vidvān yuktaḥ samācaran 3.26
Just because He is in a <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">body</span> to do this, can we say that the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> is not a mukta purusha
but a baddha jiva although a Tattvadarshi? The Vishnu sahasranama says He is:
‘Tattvavit’, and also ‘vimuktAtmA’. When the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> can be a Tattvavit and vimuktatma
why can’t a jiva who has followed the teaching of the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> and gained Tattvadarshanam
be a mukta while still in the body? Is the ParamArtha tattvam known to Bhagavan any
different from the tattvam realized by the jiva during sAkshAtkAra?
After all, the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> too, in the Rama and Krishna incarnations, was <span class="t9 t24 hoverable">born</span> from a Mother’s
womb. He too grew up from childhood to adulthood. He too ate and slept. He too
experienced pleasure and pain. In the <span class="t5 t16 t21 t24 t25 hoverable">case</span> of Krishna, He too departed from this <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">world</span>
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">upon</span> being injured by an archer/hunter. Was Krishna not a mukta purusha and still a
Tattvavit while in the Krishna-body?
The Kathopanishad says:
…..Vimuktashcha vimuchyate..(II.ii.1)
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Upon</span> realizing the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Truth</span> the aspirant is liberated – vimuktaH. The liberated one is never
<span class="t9 t24 hoverable">born</span> again – vimuchyate. The Upanishad says: <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">upon</span> realization he lives as a mukta.
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Upon</span> the fall of the body, he does not transmigrate and <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">therefore</span> does not <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">take</span> a birth
again. He is liberated for ever.

[A possible objection: ‘The <span class="t0 t1 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Divine</span> Incarnations cannot be <span class="t2 t5 t11 t18 t19 t23 t26 hoverable">taken</span> up for comparison with
the Jivanmuktas. ‘Can a Jivanmukta fight single-handedly like <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> Rama did when He
engaged in a combat the 14,000-strong army of Khara, DhUshana and Trishiras in
Janasthaanam, Dandakaranya?’ This objection is considered already in an earlier
paragraph while discussing the ‘identity’ of Jiva and <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> in the context of upadhis.]
Objection:
//If they do, then we have to either reject the Realization that is said to have occurred, or
else reject the notion that the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">world</span> of perception, as manifesting through the
attachments on a supposedly Realized person, can be sublated. In either instance, the
notion of jîvanmukti is not meaningful. //

40
Reply:
As we saw above, the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> as Sri Rama and Sri Krishna did experience pain and pleasure
in their lives. They did <span class="t6 hoverable">eat</span> and sleep. If these are the parameters to judge <span class="t0 t5 t8 t10 t14 t15 t21 t24 t28 hoverable">whether</span> a
tattvavit is a mukta or not, then we have to question the realization of Sri Rama and
Krishna and put them under the ‘supposedly Realized persons’ category. For, the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">world</span>
that the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> said ‘does not inhere in Me = na cha matsthAni bhUtAni’ (in other words,
‘remains sublated’) did <span class="t3 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t12 t13 t17 t18 t19 t20 t22 t23 t27 t29 hoverable">bring</span> pain and pleasure to Him.
The shastra says: ‘na tasya prAnaaH utkrAmanti….’. Aparoksha jnanam and the
jivanmukti that results give a guarantee to the Jnani the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">truth</span> of this mantra. He knows by
direct realization of the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Truth</span> that he is amaraNadharmaa. If the tattvadarshi believes
that he will become mukta only after death, this mantra is invalid, aprAmANika.
Therefore, for the rule ‘JnAnaan MokshaH’ to be true, jivanmukti has to be admitted.
The Chandogya Upanishat (VI.14.2): ‘tasya tAvadeva chiram…’[there is delay only till
such <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">time</span> as the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">body</span> ceases to exist] teaches the released <span class="t0 t1 t10 t14 t21 t23 t25 t29 hoverable">state</span> even while alive where
experience of the residual karma is admitted. That there is no further perpetuation of
samsara after the fall of this body, in which the Atmajnana dawned, is clear from the
‘eva’ of the mantra.
Here is a fine <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">verse</span> from the SrImadbhagavatam, Prahlada charitram:
Naarada uvAcha:
nindana-stava-satkAra-nyakkArArtham kalevaram |
pradhAna-parayO rAjan avivekena kalpitam || Canto <span class="t0 t4 t5 t8 t12 t13 t15 t18 t23 t24 t26 t28 hoverable">VII</span> . Ch.1. <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">verse</span>
['This <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">body</span> has been concocted, imagined, owing to the
non-discrimination between the Supreme <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> and Maya, the Prakriti.
What is the result of this concoction? The <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">body</span> is subjected to
insults, praise, honour and dishonour. [The teaching is: If one
continues to identify with the body, one will have to pay the
price....of these dualities.]

The above <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">verse</span> is significant in that it teaches that the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">body</span> is a product of imagination,
kalpana, <span class="t9 t24 hoverable">born</span> out of aviveka. The Aproksha jnani has freed himself from this aviveka
and realized that the prakriti-born <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">body</span> is not his Self as per the Gita (13.34):
kshetra-kshetrajnayorevam antaram jnAnachakshushA |
BhUtaprakriti-moksham cha ye viduryAnti te param ||
This is what is conveyed by the AdhyAsabhashya.
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Therefore</span> the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">body</span> is anatma. Since his identification with the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">body</span> has ceased, the
insults, praise, etc. pertaining to the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">body</span> are seen as anatma, mithya, by him.
Closely connected with the above Bhagavatam verse, we have this line from the same
source:

41
Ishwaro jIvakalayA praviShTo bhagavAniti |[Canto 3; Chapt. 29; <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">verse</span> 34; line 2]
Ishwara, the Supreme Self, has entered this <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">body</span> in the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">form</span> of the jiva, <span class="t22 t25 hoverable">individual</span> self.
This line of the Bhagavatam teaches that the jiva, in truth, is Ishwara. There are several
Shruti vakyams that teach that it is Ishwara Himself that is appearing as the jiva. For
example, the Chandogya Upanishat VI.iii.2 says: ‘anena jIvena AtmanA anu-pravishya
…. ‘ [Let me enter in the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">form</span> of the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">soul</span> of each <span class="t22 t25 hoverable">individual</span> being ….]
ajAyamAno bahudhA vijAyate [He who is never born, takes birth as multifarious
beings…] says the Purusha sUktam.
Objection: The above line of the ‘Bhagavatam’ does not mean that the jiva is in <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">truth</span>
Ishwara, for, the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">word</span> ‘jIvakalayA’ only means that the jiva is an amsha of Ishwara. The
Bhagavadgita verse: Mamaivaamsho jIvaloke jIvabhUtaH sanaatanaH….of the 15th ch.
also clearly says that the jiva is only an amsha of Ishwara.
Reply: Even <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">though</span> ‘kalaa’ has the <span class="t0 t1 t7 t12 t13 t14 t17 t23 t27 t28 hoverable">sense</span> of ‘amsha’, we should not be taking the
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t10 t12 t13 t14 t15 t17 t20 t21 t23 t24 t25 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">meaning</span> of ‘part/aspect’ in both the verses above. There is the Shruti: ‘Nishkalam
nishkriyam shAntam…’ (Shvetashwataropanishat VI.19) which says the Atman/Brahman
is Impartite. Parts/aspects in the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> that is Impartite is inadmissible. Yukti: If
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> were to be admitted as consisting of parts, He <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">would</span> be liable to destruction
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">upon</span> the disintegration of parts. So, the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t10 t12 t13 t14 t15 t17 t20 t21 t23 t24 t25 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">meaning</span> of ‘amsha’ or ‘kala’ is to be <span class="t2 t5 t11 t18 t19 t23 t26 hoverable">taken</span> as a
reflection of the Supreme in the upadhi namely the antahkaranam. This <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">would</span> be the
correct <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">way</span> to see the jiva because when the jiva realizes his <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">true</span> <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">nature</span> as the bimba,
Brahman, the upadhi <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">called</span> the antahkaranam will be known to be unreal and the ‘amsha’
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">nature</span> of jiva is no more present. Thus, amshatva is only a figurative expression for the
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> available in the antahkarana upadhi <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">called</span> jiva. Anubhava: Vidwad anubhava
is also of the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">nature</span> of ‘aham pUrNaH’ and not ‘aham amshaH’. The Shrutis ‘aham
brahmAsmi’, ‘Tat tvam asi’, ‘Atmaivedam sarvam’ ‘Brahma veda Brahmaiva bhavati’,
etc. are the authority in this regard. The declarations of the jnani-s in the Tatittiriya
Upanishat, for example, is also authority in this regard. The pUrNatva he realizes is in
tune with the description of <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> given in the Mundaka Upanishad (II.ii.11):
Brahmaivedam amrutam purastAt, Brahma pashchAt,….’ etc. This mantra teaches that
the ‘idam’ that we see as the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">world</span> all over is none other than Brahman. This is also the
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t10 t12 t13 t14 t15 t17 t20 t21 t23 t24 t25 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">meaning</span> of the Gita verse: abhito BrahmanirvANam vartate viditAtmanAm: ‘The
enlightened Jnanins experience the All-pervading Brahman.’ <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> alone appears to
the deluded intellect as the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">world</span> just like a rope appearing as a snake.
That <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">True</span> Realization is marked by the unique feeling of ‘release’ from samsara is
unmistakable for the <span class="t0 t4 t5 t10 t22 t25 t28 hoverable">person</span> who has that Realization and that <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">therefore</span> such a <span class="t0 t1 t10 t14 t21 t23 t25 t29 hoverable">state</span> of
moksha while alive is undeniable -- is <span class="t1 t3 t4 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t13 t15 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t27 t29 hoverable">brought</span> out by this <span class="t28 hoverable">passage</span> of the Aitareya
Upanishad with regard to the Realization of and its expression by Vamadeva:
//garbhe nu sannanveShAm avedam aham devAnAm janimAni vishvA shatam mA pura
AyasIr-arakShannadhaH shyeno jvasaa niradEyam iti. Garbha eva etat shayano
vAmadeva evam uvaacha.// (II.1.5)

42
Translation: // ‘While still in the womb of my mother I obtained the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">knowledge</span> of all the
births of these gods. Hundred numerous citadels, bodies, of iron, that is, as if made of
iron, held me. Then forcefully by the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">power</span> <span class="t9 t24 hoverable">born</span> of <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Knowledge</span> I came out like a
hawk tearing through a net.’ Vamadeva said this in this manner while remaining in
the womb itself.//

Objection: It is improper to say that the jiva in <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">truth</span> is Ishwara Himself. The Mundaka
mantra (III.i.1): dvA suparna…..clearly distinguishes the jiva and Ishwara as different
entities.
Reply: While this is what appears to be the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t10 t12 t13 t14 t15 t17 t20 t21 t23 t24 t25 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">meaning</span> of that mantra, one has to look at the
mantra in a larger context.
Supposing a <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">man</span> has seen a snake in the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">place</span> where actually only a rope is there. When
he reports to another <span class="t0 t4 t5 t10 t22 t25 t28 hoverable">person</span> about his ‘sighting’ a snake and its ‘presence’ there, he is
actually under the belief that the snake ‘is’ there. Now, supposing the other <span class="t0 t4 t5 t10 t22 t25 t28 hoverable">person</span> who
is familiar with that spot knows for sure that it is only a rope <span class="t1 t7 t12 t29 hoverable">left</span> behind by some
workers, he tries to convince the deluded <span class="t0 t4 t5 t10 t22 t25 t28 hoverable">person</span> about the truth.
Where is the snake?
There, in that spot.
No, it is not a snake. It is a rope.
No, it is indeed a snake; I could not have mistaken.
OK. Let us go to the spot where (you say) the snake is and verify.
So, they go to the spot; the deluded <span class="t0 t4 t5 t10 t22 t25 t28 hoverable">person</span> holding that the snake ‘is’ there and the other
one only seemingly agreeing that it is there. He knows that there are no ‘two’ entities
there: a rope and a snake. He knows that the illusory snake cannot be counted as another
entity after the only entity, the rope. If he says categorically ‘the snake is not there, it is a
rope,’ as he did say, the deluded one is not going to <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">take</span> it; he is not mentally prepared to
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">take</span> the truth. He is in need of further instruction. Until the further instruction is given,
by showing the truth, the instructor has to appear to be in agreement; for that message is
conveyed to the deluded <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">man</span> by the very agreeing to go to the spot.
What we have in the Mundaka mantra cited above is similar to this example. The Shruti
knows that there are no ‘two’ entities in the body-tree. The illusory ‘jiva’-bird cannot be
counted along with the Sakshi-bird. The ‘paramam sAmyam’, the aikyam, that the Shruti
teaches in the subsequent mantras of the Mundaka Upanishad is ample proof for the
Shruti not holding the bhokta-bird as absolutely real.[Reference to the Gita 15.10 and 11
verses discussed above could be made for clarification on this point.] The mithya cannot
be counted along with the satyam. The ‘sAmyam’ mentioned here could be understood in
the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">light</span> of ‘nirdosham hi samam brahma’, ‘samam sarvatra pashyan samavasthitam
Ishwaram’, ‘samam sarveshu bhUteshu… ‘ of the Bhagavad Gita. ‘SAmyam’ can mean
identity only for the Shruti denies any ‘other’ entity that is equal to or like Brahman:
Na tat samashcha abhyadhikashcha drishyate

43
Na tasya pratimA asti

(Shvetashvataropanishat VI.8 and IV.19)

The Shruti cannot in one go demolish the jiva-identity. It accepts, as it were,
(abhyupetya) initially, that jiva is a separate entity entangled in samsara. So it specifies
that these are the ‘two’ birds in the body-tree. Once the jiva starts ‘gazing’ at the Sakshi,
under the teaching of the proper Guru, the Guide, the sadhana will progress and
culminate in his gradually giving up his ‘separate’ identity and appreciate the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Truth</span> of the
secondless Unity of the Sakshi. The subsequent mantras of the ‘dvaa-suparna’ teach
exactly this.
The earlier cited Bhagavatam <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">verse</span> teaches that the mind-body complex is unreal. The
ultimate message we get from the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">two</span> Bhagavatam verses is: When the jiva is separated,
as taught in the Kshetra adhyaya, from the mind-body complex, what remains is One
(Supreme) Self alone; there is nothing to identify someone as ‘jiva’. This conclusion is
relevant in the context of jivanmukti while discussing the ‘unreality’ of the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">world</span> of
perception. The <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">words</span> ‘kalpitam avivekena’ of the earlier Bhagavatam <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">verse</span> is of
particular significance.
Why is the ‘dvA suparNa’ mantra not pAramArthika ?

The mantra occurs in the Mundakopanishat III.3.1.
In this mantra the jiva is shown as the karma-phala bhOkta, the experiencer of the fruits
of his karma. When we look at the teaching about the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">true</span> <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">nature</span> of the jeeva, as taught
in the Bhagavadgita, for example, we know that the jiva is not born, does not die, etc.
For an entity that has no birth at all, there cannot be the mind, prana, <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">body</span> apparatus (all
evolutes of prakriti, kshetram, from which one has to discriminate oneself and become
free). It is possible to have ignorance, desire, action, karma, fruit of karma, experiencing
of the fruit etc., only when this apparatus is available. But in this mantra we have the
jiva portrayed as not someone who is <span class="t1 t8 hoverable">free</span> from birth and <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">death</span> but who is in samsara.
This itself shows that the jiva as a samsari spoken of here is not the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">true</span> <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">nature</span> of the jiva.
But everyone in ignorance experiences to be a samsari. This unenquired-into experience
of everyone is being alluded to in this mantra and hence it is only a depiction of the
vyavaharika <span class="t0 t1 t10 t14 t21 t23 t25 t29 hoverable">state</span> and not the absolute <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Truth</span> of the jiva.
No system that promises moksha to the jiva has for its goal the retention of the above
samsaric bhokta <span class="t0 t1 t10 t14 t21 t23 t25 t29 hoverable">state</span> of the jiva. All systems endeavour to portray the jiva as <span class="t1 t8 hoverable">free</span> from
samsara. This is the pAramArthika state. This free-of-samsara <span class="t0 t1 t10 t14 t21 t23 t25 t29 hoverable">state</span> of the jiva is what is
taught in the subsequent mantras. That is one <span class="t1 t11 t16 t20 t25 t27 t28 hoverable">reason</span> why the mantra ‘dvaa suparna’ is
not the one teaching the absolutely <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">true</span> <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">nature</span> of the jiva but only the depiction of the
vyavaharic state.
When the separation from the kshetram is successfully accomplished, the realization that
one is no different from the ‘Other’ bird, Paramaatman, is had. For, when the kshetram

44
is separated, there will be nothing to finitize the Atman and consider It to be different
from the ParamAtman.
Moreover, the mantra speaks of the ‘body’ tree where the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">two</span> birds, Paramaatma and
jeevaatma, are perched, as it were. In the <span class="t0 t1 t10 t14 t21 t23 t25 t29 hoverable">state</span> of moksha no <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">body</span> will be there for the
mukta for the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">two</span> birds to be located. There will be no <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">way</span> of specifying <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">two</span> birds or
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">two</span> entities the Para and jeeva Atmans. If it is held that there will still be a body, then
that will be no moksha at all for the freedom from prakriti <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">would</span> not have been
accomplished. For this <span class="t1 t11 t16 t20 t25 t27 t28 hoverable">reason</span> too, the ‘dvaa suparna’ imagery is not absolute but only a
temporary acceptance, abhyupetya, by the Shruti.
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Yet</span> another <span class="t1 t11 t16 t20 t25 t27 t28 hoverable">reason</span> as to why this can be only an imagery and not the paramaartha tattva:
The mantra says the jeeva bird is busy experiencing karma phala. This can happen only
in the realm of artha, kaama and dharma purusharthas. But in Moksha purushartha, the
very purpose of which is to <span class="t1 t8 hoverable">free</span> the jeeva from the earlier cycle of samsara of the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">three</span>
other lower purusharthas, there will be no bhoga-bhogya-bhokta triputee (triad). So the
jeeva is just one Pure <span class="t0 t1 t13 t16 t24 t25 hoverable">Consciousness</span> freed from all bhoga instruments and bhoga objects.
This is taught by the subsequent <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">two</span> mantras culminating in the ‘paramam sAmyam’.
*****

svaeR=ip VyvharStu äü[a i³yte jnE>,

[At all times, by all people, all vyavahara is done only ‘with’ Brahman. Owing to
ignorance <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">people</span> do not realize this.* The <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Truth</span> is akin to seeing all earthenware as nondifferent from its material cause, earth. The gloss, ‘dIpikaa’, by Sri Vidyaranya Swamin on the above <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">verse</span> is:

*[To put it in a crude manner, the teaching of the Gita verse: ‘BrahmArpraNam Brahma

The following Shruti <span class="t28 hoverable">passage</span> (Ref.?) too teaches that the jivanmukta has eyes, etc. but is
as <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">though</span> <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">without</span> them. The Gita teachings seen above like ‘navadvāre pure dehī naiva

[Even <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">though</span> he is endowed with eyes, ears, mind, prana, etc., it is as <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">though</span> he is bereft of
eyes, ears, mind, prana, etc.] (Sri Bhagavatpada quotes this <span class="t28 hoverable">passage</span> in the Bhashyam for

The Brihadaranyaka Upanishad IV.iv.7 says:

//7. "Regarding this there are the following verses: "When all the desires that

away, on an ant—hill, even so lies this body. Then the self becomes disembodied and
immortal Spirit, the Supreme Self (Prana), Brahman, the Light." Janaka, Emperor of
Videha, said: "I give you, venerable Sir, a <span class="t6 hoverable">thousand</span> cows." //
The Ishavasya Upanishad 7 says:
//Yasmin sarvAni bhUtAni…
To the seer, all <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">things</span> have verily become the Self: what delusion, what sorrow, can
there be for him who beholds that oneness? //
The above Upanishads convey the message that release from
desires/delusion/sorrow is what is meant by liberation from samsara. The liberated
<span class="t0 t1 t10 t14 t21 t23 t25 t29 hoverable">state</span> is experienced here, in this <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">body</span> itself, by those Jnanis who have secured the
aparoksha jnanam.
[The Bhagavadgita II <span class="t0 t2 t3 t4 t5 t8 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t20 t21 t23 t24 t26 t27 t28 hoverable">chapter</span> verse: prajahAti yadA kAmAn sarvAn pArtha
manogatAn…specifying the sthitaprajna lakshana is the reflection of the above Shruti
passages. This is the jivanmukta lakshana.]
Is experience a proof for reality?
In normal parlance, that is, vyavahara, it is held that what is experienced is a proof
for the reality of the experience. Since this rule does not hold <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">good</span> in the field of
Absolute Reality, the transcendtal realm, the Scripture teaches the aspirant to
question this rule and grow out of this misconception.
For example, all of us believe that we are born, grow, perform actions, get old, suffer
disease, experience joy and sorrow and finally die. Those who are believers hold
that we transmigrate and are <span class="t9 t24 hoverable">born</span> again. While this is the common thinking, the
Bhagavadgita, for example, teaches us something that is quite contrary to this
thinking. In the <span class="t0 t2 t5 t13 t14 t16 t17 t20 t23 t24 t26 t28 t29 hoverable">Second</span> <span class="t0 t2 t3 t4 t5 t8 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t20 t21 t23 t24 t26 t27 t28 hoverable">Chapter</span> the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> teaches that we, the Consciousness, are
never <span class="t9 t24 hoverable">born</span> and we never die. We are never destroyed/destroyable by any force in
the creation. In the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">III</span> ch. He teaches that we are not the doers of any action; only
the prakriti, Maya, does everything. ‘The Atma is akartaa’ teach the 13th and 14th
chapters. While we think we are many, distinct, entities, the Gita teaches that the
right vision is the seeing of the One Conscious Principle in all the seemingly distinct
bodies. It censures the seeing of difference as rajasic and tamasic.
The 15th ch. <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">verse</span> ‘utkrAmantam…..’ also proves that contrary to our experience of
an embodied life, the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Truth</span> is that we are the asanga, asamsaari Atman.

46

Thus, quite contrary to our thinking that experience is a proof of reality, the
scriptures teach that this thinking is incorrect.

Objection:

Why does Tattvavâda deny jîvan-mukti?
//Because a mukta, or liberated person, should not even be physically present in the
material universe, unlike the un-liberated. A <span class="t0 t4 t5 t10 t22 t25 t28 hoverable">person</span> who is living in the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">world</span> cannot be
said to be <span class="t1 t8 hoverable">free</span> of sorrow <span class="t9 t24 hoverable">born</span> of material contact, and also cannot be said to experience
the joy of his own <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">nature</span> at all times. The very act of living in a gross material <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">body</span>
entails <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">things</span> such as eating, sleeping, pleasure and pain, etc., which cannot be accepted
in a mukta.
Here is a reply to the above:
The Upanishad teaches ‘The knower of <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> is Brahman’ ‘Brahma veda Brahmaiva’
(Mundaka). In the Srivishnusahasranama we have a name: ‘Brahmavit’, ‘AnandaH’, etc..
If it is contended that while in the gross <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">body</span> one (a Tattvadarshi) cannot experience the
svarupa-ananda at all times, we will have to conclude that Bhagavan, as Sri Rama and Sri
Krishna, was devoid of svarupa-ananda during the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">time</span> of these incarnations. If it is said
that a Brahmavit is different from Brahman, there will be contradiction to the Shruti
vakyam quoted above and also the absurd consequence of Vishnu, Brahman, being
different from Himself (Brahmavit).
In the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">light</span> of the above, we have to admit that the Brahmavit, Jivanmukta, being nondifferent from Brahman, does experience His svarupa-ananda while in the body. The
Acharyapaada makes an observation in the Taittiriya Bhashyam on ‘raso vai saH…(II.7):
bAhyAnanda-sAdhana-rahitA api nirIhA nireShaNA .brAhmanAH bAhyarasalAbhAdiva sAnandaa dRShyante vidvAmsaH, nUnam brahmaiva rasaH teShAm.
//The Brahmavits are seen to be ever-satisfied with the Ananda of their nature, svarupa,
as <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">though</span> they are deriving the joy from external objects. These Tattvadarshis are <span class="t1 t8 hoverable">free</span>
from desire. It is certain that <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> alone is the ‘rasa’ of these Jnanis. //
Arjuna uvāca
sthitaprajñasya kā bhāṣā samādhisthasya keśava
sthitadhīḥ kiṃ prabhāṣeta kim āsīta vrajeta kim 2.54
śrībhagavān uvāca

47
prajahāti yadā kāmān sarvān pārtha manogatān
ātmany evātmanā tuṣṭaḥ sthitaprajñas tadocyate 2.55
The above Gita verses make it clear that the Tattvadarshi is <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">called</span> a sthitaprajna, a <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">man</span> of
steady <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">knowledge</span> of the Truth, when he is all with his Self, reveling in the joy of the
Atman. This is svarupa ananda anubhava. If this <span class="t0 t1 t10 t14 t21 t23 t25 t29 hoverable">state</span> were only a temporary one, the
jnani will not be <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">called</span> a sthita-prajna. The prajnaa-sthairya <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">would</span> be meaningful only
when the tushti is available to him always.
In the <span class="t26 hoverable">third</span> chapter, we have:
yas tv ātmaratir eva syād ātmatṛptaś ca mānavaḥ
ātmany eva ca saṃtuṣṭas tasya kāryaṃ na vidyate 3.17
naiva tasya kṛtenārtho nākṛteneha kaścana
na cāsya sarvabhūteṣu kaścid arthavyapāśrayaḥ 3.18
na me pārthāsti kartavyaṃ triṣu lokeṣu kiṃcana
nānavāptam avāptavyaṃ varta eva ca karmaṇi 3.22
In the above verses too, we have the proof of jivanmukti. The <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> says that this
‘manavaH’, a <span class="t0 t1 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">human</span> being in gross body, is always turned towards the Atman bliss and
derives <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">great</span> satisfaction, tripti, from this svarupa ananda. Such a <span class="t0 t4 t5 t10 t22 t25 t28 hoverable">person</span> has nothing to
accomplish in the world. What else is this if not jivanmukti? Here is a clear instance of
the Tattvadarshi remaining in the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">body</span> and still enjoying the Svarupa ananda; there is no
need to die for this. The <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> further emphasizes that this <span class="t0 t1 t10 t14 t21 t23 t25 t29 hoverable">state</span> of the jivanmukta is no
different from His (the Lord’s) own <span class="t0 t1 t10 t14 t21 t23 t25 t29 hoverable">state</span> (3.22) wherein the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> is (also) <span class="t1 t8 hoverable">free</span> from any
‘kartavyam’. This freedom from ‘kartavyam’ is undoubtedly the result of the Lord’s own
ever-subsisting svarupa ananda anubhava. That an ignorant <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">man</span> is compelled to act is a
consequence of his ignorance of his svAbhAvika pUrnatva is undoubtedly admitted by
all. The Jnani who has realized his pUrnatva is spoken of by the Gita thus:
yAvaanartha udapAne sarvataHsamplutodake |
tAvAn sarveShu vedeShu brAhmaNasya vijAnataH || (2.46)
Again compare the above with the Lord’s declaration of His own PUrNatva and the
consequent transcendence from ‘compelled kartavyatva’ (3.22).
sukham ātyantikaṃ yat tad buddhigrāhyam atīndriyam
vetti yatra na caivāyaṃ sthitaś calati tattvataḥ 6.21
yaṃ labdhvā cāparaṃ lābhaṃ manyate nādhikaṃ tataḥ
yasmin sthito na duḥkhena guruṇāpi vicālyate 6.22

48
taṃ vidyād.h duḥkhasaṃyogaviyogaṃ yogasaṃjñitam
sa niścayena yoktavyo yogonirviṇṇacetasā 6.23
praśāntamanasaṃ hy enaṃ yoginaṃ sukham uttamam
upaiti śāntarajasaṃ brahmabhūtam akalmaṣam 6.27
yuñjann evaṃ sadātmānaṃ yogī vigatakalmaṣaḥ
sukhena brahmasaṃsparśam atyantaṃ sukham aśnute 6.28
yo māṃ paśyati sarvatra sarvaṃ ca mayi paśyati
tasyāhaṃ na praṇaśyāmi sa ca me na praṇaśyati 6.30
The highlighted portions <span class="t6 t9 t11 t19 t20 t22 hoverable">speak</span> for themselves the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">nature</span> of the bliss enjoyed by the
Tattvadarshi, even while living in the body. The bliss is the Greatest, verily the bliss of
Brahman. What more proof is needed to show that the svarupa Ananda is experienced by
the Tattvadarshi, jivanmukta, while in the gross body? The ‘sarvAtmatva drishti’ gained
by the Jnani enables him to have the <span class="t0 t1 t13 t16 t24 t25 hoverable">Consciousness</span> of the Self at all times; it is never lost
to him. The last quoted <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">verse</span> above teaches this. The ‘sarvatra Atma darshanam’ can be
possible only when the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">body</span> is alive and the senses perceive the variety. This is
jivanmukti.
CONCLUSION
The core teaching of the Bhagavadgita begins from the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">verse</span> 2.11:
śrībhagavān uvāca
aśocyān anvaśocas tvaṃ prajñāvādāṃś ca bhāṣase
gatāsūn agatāsūṃś ca nānuśocanti paṇḍitāḥ 2.11
From this seminal teaching we understand:
1. To grieve for those alive and those who have departed is ignorance.
2. It is ignorance because whatever happens to those who live is happening to the
body-mind complex and not to the Atman. Likewise, <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">death</span> occurs to the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">body</span>
only and not to the Atman.
3. The <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> teaches that the Atman is ‘na jAyate’ (never born), ‘na mriyate’ (never
dies).
4. Everyone knows that a <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">body</span> is assigned only if it is born.
5. Since Atman is never born, It is different from the body; it cannot possess a body.
6. The <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> teaches that we are the Atman in <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">truth</span> and not the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">body</span> which is not our
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">true</span> self. <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Therefore</span> the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> says that to grieve for both those alive and the dead
is ignorance. It is only because we have ‘taken’ ourselves to be the body-mind
that we grieve for what happens to the body-mind. The Scriptures endeavor to
correct this mistake. To think that we are the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">body</span> is ignorance, ajnana, avidya.
To gain the <span class="t7 t8 t12 hoverable">wisdom</span> that we are the Atman and not the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">body</span> is jnana, vidya.

49
7. That which is corrected by vidya, jnana, is ajnana, avidya. The ‘we-are-the-body’
(and <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">therefore</span> finite) <span class="t0 hoverable">idea</span> is corrected by the jnana ‘I am the Atman’ (and
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">therefore</span> am the Infinite Brahman) .Hence the body-idea is Avidyaka. It could be
objected: What is corrected by <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">knowledge</span> need not be unreal. It could very <span class="t0 t1 t3 t4 t5 t6 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">well</span>
be anitya. To grieve for something that is anitya is ignorance and this is what is
corrected by the scripture. To this the reply is: ‘anitya’ by definition is something
that was not there before and will not be there later but is there only in the present.
That which is absent before and after is deemed to be absent even in the
intervening present. Ultimately, ‘anitya’ is not different from ‘mithya’. The
following <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">two</span> closely connected verses of the Gita Ch.II could be studied:
mātrāsparśās tu kaunteya śītoṣṇasukhaduḥkhadāḥ
āgamāpāyinonityās tāṃs titikṣasva bhārata 2.14
nāsato vidyate bhāvo nābhāvo vidyate sataḥ
ubhayor api dṛṣṭo.antas tv anayos tattvadarśibhiḥ 2.16
While the former talks about ‘anityatva’, the latter teaches the mithyAtva of
phenomena. Both the verses occur in the context of forbearance, titikshA.
Forbearance is on stronger ground when one realizes that the phenomena encountered
are not real and they are only appearing to be present. Their ‘asat’ <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">nature</span> when
realized brings about greater peace of <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">mind</span> and renders the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">mind</span> more conducive for
‘tattva dharshanam’.
8. All those who accept that the Atman is different from the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">body</span> have to admit that
the body-idea is <span class="t9 t24 hoverable">born</span> of ignorance. Since Jnana corrects this ignorance and since
this happens when one is alive, it has to be logically concluded that the body-idea
is only a superimposition on the Atman. And the superimposition goes when
right <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">knowledge</span> of the Atman arises. Since the scriptures do not say that the
dawn of right <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">knowledge</span> is coeval with the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">death</span> of the body, and since
samsaritva is terminated by right knowledge, the <span class="t0 t1 t10 t14 t21 t23 t25 t29 hoverable">state</span> of the Jnani is the liberated
state, moksha.
9. To remain in the body-idea is samsara. Samsara is karta-bhokta bhava. This is
what is amply borne out by the ‘dvaa-suparna’ mantra of the Mundaka Upanishad
and the ‘utkrAmantam shtitam vAapi….’ <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">verse</span> of the Gita 15th ch. He who is a
samsari is <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">called</span> a jiva.
10. The <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> teaches that the Atman is akarta-abhokta. <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Therefore</span> the Atman is not a
jiva, samsari.The Jnani has discarded the body-idea. He has <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">thus</span> freed himself
from samsara and is <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">therefore</span> a mukta.
11. That such is the <span class="t5 t16 t21 t24 t25 hoverable">case</span> is taught by the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> in the verses: The jnani knows that he
is not the doer/enjoyer ‘naiva kinchit karomi…’even while the <span class="t0 t1 t7 t12 t13 t14 t17 t23 t27 t28 hoverable">sense</span> organs are
operating, ‘pashyan, shrunvan, etc.’ This is said by the Shruti vakyam: 'sachakshurachakshuriva, sa-karno'karna iva, sa-manA amanA iva, sa-prANo'prAna
iva'. [even <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">though</span> he is with eyes, ears, etc., he is as <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">though</span> <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">without</span> them.’]
12. In the said Gita verses: naiva kinchit karomi…..the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> is teaching that the
world/body that is sublated by samyagdarshanam will continue for some <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">time</span> till

50
the fall of the body. This is called: bAdhita-anuvritti. The bodily functions and
interaction of the senses with the objects will continue due to the past momentum
but the Jivanmukta himself will remain disassociated from them. This is what is
conveyed by the words: pashyan, shrunvan, etc. of the Gita.
13. Since the Jnani’s identification with the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">body</span> has ceased, he is actually ‘asharIri’.
This is said in the Chandogya Upanishad (VIII.12.1): ‘ashrIram vaa va santam na
priya-apriye sprushataH’ [That which is bereft of body-identification is untouched
by joy and sorrow.] Being afflicted by joy and sorrow is samsara (ref: dvaa
suparnaa). Freedom from joy-sorrow is what moksha is: paramam sAmyam.
14. The Brihadaranyaka mantra (IV.iv.13) ‘Atmaanam ched vijAnIyAt ‘ayam asmi’
iti pUruShaH, kim icchan kasya kAmAya sharIram anu sanjvaret’ is relevant in
this context. ‘If a <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">man</span> knows the Self as ‘I am this’, then desiring what and for
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t11 t12 t13 t14 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">whose</span> sake will he suffer in the wake of the body?’ <span class="t0 t10 t11 t17 t25 t28 t29 hoverable">Desire</span> for attaining
something and avoiding something is what is denoted by samsara. When
someone transcends this by right knowledge, the connection with the body-idea
ceases. The right <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">knowledge</span> gained is that of one’s pUrNatva. This <span class="t0 t1 t10 t14 t21 t23 t25 t29 hoverable">state</span> is <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">called</span>
‘tripti’. When a <span class="t0 t4 t5 t10 t22 t25 t28 hoverable">person</span> has no <span class="t0 t10 t11 t17 t25 t28 t29 hoverable">desire</span> <span class="t9 t24 hoverable">born</span> out of ignorance, he is stated to be
sated completely. Swami Vidyaranya writes one <span class="t10 t16 hoverable">full</span> <span class="t0 t2 t3 t4 t5 t8 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t20 t21 t23 t24 t26 t27 t28 hoverable">chapter</span> of 298 verses in the
Panchadashi under the title ‘Tripti Deepa prakaranam’ expounding the deep
purport of this mantra. The Gita too teaches that the Jnani is ‘nitya tripta’ and
does not depend on anything in the world. This is <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">called</span> Jivanmukti. That the
‘svarUpa Ananda’ is experienced by the Jnani (while living) is also borne out by
the Gita.
15. To put the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t29 hoverable">whole</span> <span class="t3 t5 t6 t7 t10 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t25 t28 t29 hoverable">thing</span> in a nut-shell: (a) freedom from samsara (b) experience of
tripti and (c) experience of svarupa ananda which are the hallmarks of moksha
can be had while the <span class="t0 t4 t5 t10 t22 t25 t28 hoverable">person</span> is alive. The Shruti, smriti, yukti and vidwadanubhava are all pramanas for this. If someone questions/denies Jivanmukti it is
evident that: (1) he has not understood the purport of the moksha shastra (2) has
not had genuine Aupanishada advaita Atma sAkshAtkara. Jivan mukti is an
undeniable <span class="t7 t12 t13 hoverable">fact</span> of experience to the one who has had the direct realization of the
Atman/Brahman. Says Bhagavatpada Shankara in the Bhashyam on Brahma
Sutra (IV.1.15):

ÎºlÉiÉ|ÉYÉ±ÉIÉhÉÊxÉnæù¶ÉäxÉ BiÉnäù´É ÊxÉ‾ûSªÉiÉä *

51
//api cha naivaatra vivaditavyam brahmavidA kanchitkAlam sharIram dhriyate na
vA dhriyate iti. Katham hi ekasya sva-hrudaya-pratyayam brahmavedanam
dehadhAraNam cha apareNa pratiksheptum shakyate? Shruti-smrutishu cha
sthitaprajnalakshana-nirdeshena etadeva niruchyate.//
[Furthermore, no difference of opinion is possible here as to <span class="t0 t5 t8 t10 t14 t15 t21 t24 t28 hoverable">whether</span> or not the
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">body</span> is retained for some period (after enlightenment) by the knowers of
Brahman. For, when somebody has the conviction in his <span class="t0 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t28 hoverable">heart</span> that he has realized
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> and <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">yet</span> retains the body, how can this be denied by anybody else? This
very <span class="t7 t12 t13 hoverable">fact</span> is elaborated in the Upanishads and Smritis in the course of determining
the characteristics of a sthitaH prajna (the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">man</span> of steady <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">knowledge</span> of the Truth)]
a-prajna or asthita-prajnatva is samsara. Sthita prajnatva denotes moksha from
samsara. The <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> speaks of the Sthitaprajna lakshanas of a mukta who is still
alive.
It <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">would</span> be pertinent to question: What prevents a Tattvadarshi from realizing that
he is a mukta? If he says/thinks that since the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">body</span> is alive he is not (yet) a
mukta, then it is evident that he has not had the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">true</span> realization. For, realization
of the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Truth</span> frees him from samsara instantly. If he thinks the fall of the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">body</span>
only will give him <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">true</span> moksha, he is <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">yet</span> to have the correct realization of the
Truth. Sri Shankaracharya has raised the objections, very similar to the ones
contained in the ‘TattvavAda’-criticism of the Vedantic <span class="t25 hoverable">view</span> of Jivanmukti, and
answered them in the Brihadaranyaka Upanishad Bhashya for the mantra: I.iv.10
where occurs the Mahavakya ‘aham BrahmAsmi’. This could be read on pages
114 onwards, especially page 116, in the English translation by
Sw.Madhavananda published by Advaita Ashrama.
The unmistakable Freedom from samsara, Moksha/Mukti, directly experienced by
the Aproksha Jnani, even while alive, as <span class="t1 t3 t4 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t13 t15 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t27 t29 hoverable">brought</span> out in the Aitareya Upanishad,
immediately <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">upon</span> obtaining the Jnanam is the incontrovertible, undeniable
Upanishadic Proof for Jivanmukti. If someone who has no such personal
experience of being freed from samsara/ajnana is considered to be a Tattvajnani
(who may or may not attain moksha after death), the Tattvajnanam had is
questionable. For, the very infallible <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">nature</span> of genuine Tattvajnanam is its
immediate fuit of clearly experienceable freedom.
‘While still in the womb of my mother I obtained the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">knowledge</span> of all the births
of these gods. Hundred numerous citadels, bodies, of iron, that is, as if made of
iron, held me. Then forcefully by the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">power</span> <span class="t9 t24 hoverable">born</span> of <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Knowledge</span> I came out
like a hawk tearing through a net.’ Vamadeva said this in this manner while
remaining in the womb itself.// (II.1.5)
The above quote is also ample proof for the <span class="t7 t12 t13 hoverable">fact</span> that the teaching of Moksha is
verifiable even while living by one who gets the Jnanam. If jivanmukti is not
accepted, one has no certainty in the occurrence of the fruit of Moksha taught by

52
the Upanishads. It is always a ‘he may attain moksha after <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">death</span> if ….conditions
are fulfilled’. Surely this sorry <span class="t0 t1 t10 t14 t21 t23 t25 t29 hoverable">state</span> of affairs is not prevalnt in the Upanishads.
Mokshashaastra is a Perfect Verifiable Science leaving no room for uncertainty,
doubt, etc. That is the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">nature</span> of the PramANa <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">called</span> the Upanishads.
Yasya prasAdAt ahameva VishNuH maiyyeva sarvam parikalpitam cha |
Ittham vijaanAmi sadAtmarUpam tasyAnghri-padme satatam namAmi ||
